The General Principle of Fosterage Prohibition
Definition and expansion of the principle of fosterage prohibitions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule that fosterage creates the same marital prohibitions as lineage and affinity, and identify which relationships become prohibited.

Core Idea
Fosterage creates the same marital prohibitions as blood lineage and affinity.

This lesson explains a foundational principle in Islamic family law: breastfeeding establishes a mahram relationship equivalent to lineage. The passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the scope of this rule, its evidence, and the few exceptions that some scholars have noted.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Rule
What is the general principle stated in the passage? The text says 'what is prohibited by lineage and affinity is prohibited by fosterage'.
This is the core teaching.
2
Examine the Proof
The rule is based on Quranic verse and hadith. The passage simply references these without quoting them. Recall that Quran 4:23 lists fosterage relationships and the hadith states 'What is prohibited by lineage is prohibited by fosterage'.
Dalil is from Quran and Sunnah.
3
Apply to Specific Cases
The text gives an example: if a woman breastfeeds a boy, the boy is prohibited from marrying the wife of the wet nurse's husband (i.e., the wet nurse herself and any other wives he has) because she becomes his father's wife by fosterage. Similarly, the wet nurse's husband cannot marry the boy's wife.
The wet nurse's husband becomes the foster father.
4
Consider Exceptions
The passage discusses that some scholars enumerate 21 cases where fosterage does not create prohibition, but the relied-upon view is that no exception is needed because the effective cause for prohibition is present in all cases.
The majority Hanafi position applies the general rule.
5
Understand the Authority
The rule is from zahir al-riwayah and is supported by authoritative scholars like al-Ramli. The text notes that the author of al-Kashshaf is a reliable source in the madhhab.
This rule is firmly established.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والكل رضاعاً) بيان للنوع الثالث وهو أن ما يحرم بالنسب والصهرية يحرم بالرضاع للآية والحديث حتى لو أرضعت امرأة صبياً حرم عليه زوجة زوج الظئر الذي نزل لبنها منه لأنها امرأة أبيه من الرضاعة، ويحرم على زوج الظئر امرأة هذا الصبي لأنها امرأة ابنه من الرضاعة. وفي شرح الوقاية : وهذا يشمل عدة أقسام كبنت الأخت مثلاً تشمل البنت الرضاعية للأخت النسبية فعزاها إليه، لأن صاحب الكشاف من مشايخ المذهب وهو حجة في النقل . قوله : (فإن أريد به حرمة امرأة الأب والجد) الذي في الفتح : فإن أريد من حرمة بلفظ من الجارة بدل «به» والمعنى عليها ظاهر . قوله : (فإن الإجماع تابع للنص أو القياس عن أحدهما يكون قال الرملي : معناه أن الإجماع لا يكون إلا عن النص أو القياس المأخوذ من النص فافهم ا هـ . فقوله عن أحدهما يكون أي يوجد وينشأ بيان للتبعية قوله : (وذكر الأصلاب في الآية الخ قال الرملي قالوا لا يحرم على المرء زوجة من تبناه لأنه ليس بابن له ولا تحرم بنت زوج الأم ولا أمه ولا أم زوجة الأب ولا بنتها ولا أم . ولم يستثن المصنف هنا شيئاً واستثنى في كتاب الرضاع أم أخيه وأخت ابنه، وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى أنه لا حاجة إليه عند المحققين لأن المعنى الذي لأجله حرم في النسب لم يكن موجوداً فيهما واستثنى بعضهم إحدى وعشرين صورة وجمعها في قوله : يفارق النسب الإرضاع في صور كأم نافلة أو جدة الولد وأم عم وأخت ابن وأم أخ وأم خال وعمـة ابـن اعـتـمــد لأن كل واحد من هذه السبع إما أن يكون المضاف رضاعياً والمضاف إليه نسبياً أو عكسه، أو كل منهما رضاعياً فيجوز له نكاح أم أخيه رضاعاً، سواء كانت الأم رضاعية وحدها أو نسبية وحدها أو كل منهما رضاعياً وكذا في بقية الصور
His statement: 'And all by fosterage' is an explanation of the third type, which is that what is prohibited by lineage and affinity is prohibited by fosterage based on the verse and hadith. So if a woman breastfeeds a boy, then the wife of the husband of the wet nurse from whose milk it came becomes prohibited to him, because she is the wife of his father by fosterage. And the husband of the wet nurse is prohibited to marry the wife of this boy, because she is the wife of his son by fosterage. In Sharh al-Wiqaya: This includes several categories, such as the daughter of the sister, for example, it includes the foster daughter of the sister by lineage, so he attributed it to him, because the author of al-Kashshaf is among the shaykhs of the madhhab and is authoritative in transmission. His statement: 'Then if it is intended by it the prohibition of the wife of the father and grandfather' - in al-Fath: then if it is intended from 'the prohibition' with the letter min instead of 'bi', and its meaning is apparent. His statement: 'Then consensus depends on the text or analogy; from one of them it occurs.' al-Ramli said: Its meaning is that consensus does not occur except from the text or from analogy derived from the text, so understand. He said his statement 'from one of them it occurs' means it exists and originates as an explanation of dependency. His statement: 'And mentioning of the loins in the verse etc.' al-Ramli said: They said: The wife of the one who adopted him is not prohibited to the man, because he is not his son. And the daughter of the stepfather is not prohibited, nor his mother, nor the mother of the father's wife, nor her daughter, nor the mother... And the author did not make an exception here of anything, but in the Book of Fosterage he excepted the mother of a brother and the sister of a son. And it will come, Allah willing, that there is no need for it according to the verified scholars, because the reason for which it is prohibited in lineage is not present in them. And some excepted twenty-one cases and collected them in his statement: Fosterage differs from lineage in cases such as the mother of a foster child or the grandmother of a child, and the maternal uncle's mother, and the sister of a son, and the mother of a brother, and the maternal uncle's mother, and the paternal aunt of a son, upon which one relies. Because each of these seven is either that the added one is by fosterage and the one to whom added is by lineage, or vice versa, or both by fosterage. So it is permissible for him to marry the mother of his brother by fosterage, whether the mother is by fosterage alone or by lineage alone or both by fosterage. And likewise in the remaining cases.
Source pages p. 167

Commentary
This passage is a definition and ruling explaining the principle that prohibitions established by lineage and affinity are also established by fosterage (rada'). It is based on the Quranic verse and hadith. The text gives examples: if a woman breastfeeds a boy, the boy is prohibited from marrying the wife of the wet nurse's husband (because she becomes his father's wife by fosterage) and the wet nurse's husband is prohibited from marrying the boy's wife (because she becomes his son's wife by fosterage). The passage then discusses exceptions: some cases where fosterage does not create prohibition. The author mentions that the compiler did not make exceptions here, but in the book of fosterage he excepted two cases. However, verified scholars say those exceptions are unnecessary. Some scholars have listed twenty-one cases where fosterage differs from lineage, and the text cites a poem that summarizes seven categories.

Key Terms
الرضاع (ar-rada'): Fosterage; breastfeeding that creates a mahram relationship.
الظئر (az-zawj az-zawj? Actually 'zawj adh-dha'r' means the husband of the wet nurse.): The husband of the wet nurse; he becomes the foster father.
mahram (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, affinity, or fosterage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Analogy to affinity

Key Takeaway
The principle that fosterage creates the same prohibitions as lineage is firmly established in the Hanafi school, with the general rule applied unless a clear exception is proven.

Prohibition of Combining Two Sisters in Marriage and Concubinage
Explaining the prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage and concubinage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on combining two sisters in marriage and milk al-yamin, and apply it to related scenarios such as fosterage and marriage with a concubine's sister.

Core Idea
It is haram to be married to or have intercourse with two sisters simultaneously, whether by marriage or concubinage.

This lesson addresses a fundamental prohibition in marriage law: combining two sisters. The ruling is explicit in the Qur'an and hadith, and it extends by analogy to fosterage and other mahram relationships. Understanding this prohibition is crucial for correct practice in marriage and slave ownership.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its prohibition
The passage prohibits combining two sisters in marriage (nikah) and intercourse (wat') by milk al-yamin. 'Combining' means having both at the same time.
The prohibition includes both marriage contracts and concubinage.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary evidence is Quran 4:23 and a hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine his water in the womb of two sisters.'
The Quranic verse explicitly forbids combining two sisters in marriage.
3
Explore the qiyas (analogy)
The prohibition extends to fosterage (rida') and other mahram relationships by qiyas, because the effective cause (illa) is the sisterhood or mahram relationship.
The analogy is based on the similarity of the relationship, not on severing the womb.
4
Apply to the case of marrying a concubine's sister
If a man owns a concubine with whom he has had intercourse, marrying her sister is valid but he must refrain from intercourse with both until he sells the first.
The marriage is valid because it issues from a capable person and is added to its proper place.
5
Understand the objection and its rebuttal
An objection claims that the concubine is considered as having intercourse by legal fiction, so the marriage becomes a combination. The rebuttal: he can remove the legal fiction by selling or freeing the concubine, so the marriage is valid.
The prohibition of intercourse is immediate, but the marriage contract itself is not invalid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والجمع بين الأختين نكاحاً ووطئاً بملك يمين) بيان للنوع الرابع وهو الجمع بين المحارم، أما الأول فلقوله تعالى ﴿وإن تجمعوا بين الأختين﴾ [النساء : ۲۳] وأما الثاني فللحديث «من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يجمعن ماءه في رحم أختين» وليس حرمة الجمع بينهما لقطع الرحم لما في المبسوط . ولا يجمع الرجل بين أختين من الرضاعة ولا بين امرأة وابنة أختها أو ابنة أخيها ، وكذلك كل امرأة ذات محرم منها من الرضاعة للأصل الذي بينا أن كل امرأتين لو كانت إحداهما ذكراً والأخرى أنثى لم يجز للذكر أن يتزوج الأنثى فإنه يحرم الجمع بينهما بالقياس على حرمة الجمع بين ا الأختين فكذلك من الرضاعة . وتبين بهذا أن حرمة هذا الجمع ليس لقطيعة الرحم فإنه ليس بين الرضيعين رحم وحرمة الجمع بينهما ثابتة ا هـ . وسيأتي حديث يرده فلو قدموا حرمة الجمع على قولهم والكل رضاعاً لكان أولى كما لا يخفى، وتفرع على عدم الفرق بين الأختين نسباً ورضاعاً أنه لو كان له زوجتان رضيعتان أرضعتهما أجنبية فسد نكاحهما، والمراد بالنكاح في المختصر العقد. وقوله «بملك يمين» متعلق بالوطء فأفاد أنه يجوز الجمع بينهما ملكاً بدون الوطء قوله : (فلو تزوج أخت أمته الموطوءة لم يطأ واحدة منهما حتى يبيعها بيان لشيئين : أحدهما صحة نكاح الأخت مع كون أختها موطوءة له بملك اليمين لصدوره من أهله مضافاً إلى محله وأورد عليه أن المنكوحة موطوءة حكماً باعترافكم فيصير بالنكاح جامعاً وطئاً حكماً وهو باطل، وجوابه أن لزوم الجمع بينهما وطئاً حكماً ليس بلازم لأن بيده إزالته فلا يضر بالصحة ويمنع من الوطء بعدها لقيامه إذا ذاك . أطلق في الأخت
His statement: 'And the combining of two sisters in marriage and intercourse by right of hand' is an explanation of the fourth type, which is combining those who are mahram. As for the first, by His statement: 'And do not combine between two sisters' [4:23]. And as for the second, by the hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine his water in the womb of two sisters.' And the prohibition of combining them is not due to severing the womb, as in al-Mabsut. A man should not combine two sisters by fosterage, nor combine a woman and her sister's daughter or brother's daughter. Likewise, every two women such that if one were male and the other female, the male would not be allowed to marry the female, then it is prohibited to combine them by analogy to the prohibition of combining two sisters, and likewise from fosterage. And it is clarified by this that the prohibition of this combination is not due to severing the womb, for there is no womb between the two foster children, yet the prohibition of combining them is established. The end. And a hadith will come that refutes it. So if they placed the prohibition of combination on their statement 'and all by fosterage', it would be more appropriate, as is not hidden. And a branch based on the absence of difference between two sisters by lineage and by fosterage: if a man has two wives who are foster sisters, both nursed by a stranger, his marriage to them is invalid. And what is meant by marriage in al-Mukhtasar is the contract. And his statement 'by right of hand' is connected to intercourse, indicating that it is permissible to combine them in ownership without intercourse. His statement: 'So if he marries the sister of his concubine with whom he has had intercourse, he should not have intercourse with either until he sells her' is an explanation of two things: one is the validity of the marriage of the sister while her sister is his concubine, because it comes from a capable person and it is added to its proper place. And it is objected: the married woman is considered to have intercourse by legal fiction because of your admission, so he would become combining intercourse legally, which is invalid. The answer: that the necessity of combining them in intercourse by legal fiction is not necessary because he can remove it, so it does not harm validity, and he is prevented from intercourse after it because it would then actually exist. He made it absolute regarding the sister.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof addressing the prohibition of concurrently being married to or having intercourse with two sisters, whether by marriage or slave concubinage. The Quranic verse and a hadith are cited. The prohibition applies to both sisters by lineage and by fosterage, and also to other combinations where if one were male and the other female they would be mahram (e.g., a woman and her niece). The passage clarifies that the prohibition is not based on kinship severity but on the text. A practical example: if a man owns a slave-woman and has intercourse with her, he may not marry her sister until he sells the first concubine. The marriage to the sister is valid but he cannot have intercourse with either until he disposes of one. The text also addresses an objection that the concubine is considered to be under intercourse by legal fiction, making the marriage a combination of intercourse—this is refuted. The passage also notes that combining in ownership alone (without intercourse) is permissible.

Key Terms
الجمع بين الأختين (al-jam' bayn al-ukhtayn): The act of being married to or having intercourse with two sisters simultaneously.
ملك يمين (milk al-yamin): Ownership of the right hand; refers to a female slave (concubine) with whom the master may have intercourse.
رضاع (rida'ah): Fosterage; the relationship created by breastfeeding, which establishes mahram status.
محرم (mahram): A person with whom marriage is permanently prohibited due to lineage, fosterage, or marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man owns a slave woman and has intercourse with her, what is the ruling on marrying her sister?
A) It is invalid because he cannot combine two sisters
B) It is valid but he must not have intercourse with either until he sells the first
C) It is valid and he may have intercourse with both alternately
D) It is invalid because the first is considered his wife

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of combining two sisters is absolute and extends to fosterage and by analogy to all women who are mahram to each other; marriage to a sister of a concubine is valid but intercourse is suspended until disposal.

Prohibition of Combining Two Sisters: Proof and Qiyas Extension
Explains the prohibition with Quran, hadith, and extension to fosterage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the evidence for the prohibition of combining two sisters in marriage and concubinage, and explain why the prohibition extends to foster-sisters via qiyas.

Core Idea
The Quran and Hadith forbid combining two sisters; the same prohibition applies to foster-sisters by qiyas.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the fourth type of prohibited marriages: combining two sisters, whether in marriage or as concubines. The author cites clear Quranic and hadith proofs and then extends the ruling to foster-sisters using qiyas. You will learn to identify the evidence, understand the rationale, and apply the ruling correctly, especially the distinction between ownership and sexual intercourse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is 'combining two sisters' (al-jam' bayna al-ukhtayn) in marriage or as concubines. The ruling is haram (prohibited).
The prohibition covers both nikah (marriage contract) and wat' (sexual intercourse) via milk al-yamin.
2
Locate the primary evidence
First evidence: Quran 4:23, which explicitly states 'And that you combine two sisters'. Second evidence: a hadith prohibiting combining one's water in the wombs of two sisters.
The Quranic verse is qat'i al-thubut wa al-dalalah (definitive in transmission and meaning).
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The verse's direct command (imperative) indicates prohibition. The hadith reinforces this by warning those who believe in Allah and the Last Day.
4
Understand the extension to foster-sisters via qiyas
The author uses qiyas: the illa (effective cause) is the mahram relationship of sisterhood, which exists in both blood and foster relations. Therefore, the prohibition applies equally to foster-sisters.
The author refutes a claim from al-Mabsut that the prohibition is due to severing the womb; foster-siblings have no womb relation yet the prohibition holds.
5
Distinguish ownership from sexual intercourse
The text clarifies that combining sisters in ownership (milk al-yamin) without sexual intercourse is permissible. The prohibition only applies to sexual access to both.
This is a key practical point often misunderstood.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والجمع بين الأختين نكاحاً ووطئاً بملك يمين) بيان للنوع الرابع وهو الجمع بين المحارم، أما الأول فلقوله تعالى وإن تجمعوا بين الأختين ﴾ [النساء : ۲۳] وأما الثاني فللحديث من كان يؤمن بالله واليوم الآخر فلا يجمعن ماءه في رحم أختين وليس حرمة الجمع بينهما لقطع الرحم لما في المبسوط . ولا يجمع الرجل بين أختين من الرضاعة ولا بين امرأة وابنة أختها أو ابنة أخيها ، وكذلك كل امرأة ذات محرم منها من الرضاعة للأصل الذي بينا أن كل امرأتين لو كانت إحداهما ذكراً والأخرى أنثى لم يجز للذكر أن يتزوج الأنثى فإنه يحرم الجمع بينهما بالقياس على حرمة الجمع بين ا الأختين فكذلك من الرضاعة . وتبين بهذا أن حرمة هذا الجمع ليس لقطيعة الرحم فإنه ليس بين الرضيعين رحم وحرمة الجمع بينهما ثابتة ا هـ . وسيأتي حديث يرده فلو قدموا حرمة الجمع على قولهم والكل رضاعاً لكان أولى كما لا يخفى، وتفرع على عدم الفرق بين الأختين نسباً ورضاعاً أنه لو كان له زوجتان رضيعتان أرضعتهما أجنبية فسد نكاحهما، والمراد بالنكاح في المختصر العقد. وقوله «بملك يمين» متعلق بالوطء فأفاد أنه يجوز الجمع بينهما ملكاً بدون الوطء
His statement: (And combining two sisters in marriage and sexual intercourse by right hand possession) is an explanation of the fourth type, which is combining prohibited relatives. As for the first, due to His statement 'And that you combine two sisters' [an-Nisa 4:23]. As for the second, due to the hadith: 'Whoever believes in Allah and the Last Day, let him not combine his water in the womb of two sisters.' The prohibition of combining them is not due to severing the womb, as in al-Mabsut. A man may not combine two sisters through fosterage, nor a woman and her sister's daughter or brother's daughter, and likewise every woman who has a mahram relationship through fosterage, based on the principle we established that if two women were such that one were male and the other female, it would not be permissible for the male to marry the female, so combining them is prohibited by qiyas on the prohibition of combining two sisters, and similarly for fosterage. By this it becomes clear that the prohibition of this combination is not due to severing the womb, because there is no womb between two foster-siblings, yet the prohibition of combining them is established. End quote. A hadith will come to refute it. If they had prioritized the prohibition of combining over their statement that both are fosterage, it would be more appropriate, as is not hidden. It branches off from the lack of difference between blood sisters and fosterage sisters that if a man has two wives who are foster-sisters, having been suckled by a foreign woman, their marriage is corrupted. What is meant by 'marriage' in al-Mukhtasar is the contract. His statement 'by right hand possession' is attached to sexual intercourse, so it indicates that combining them in ownership without sexual intercourse is permissible.
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn's ruling prohibiting combining two sisters. The author explains the fourth type of prohibited marriage: combining two sisters in marriage or as concubines. The primary evidence is Quran 4:23, which explicitly prohibits combining two sisters. Additionally, a hadith states not to combine one's water in the wombs of two sisters. The author then clarifies that the prohibition is not due to cutting off kinship ties (as some might think) because it also applies to foster-sisters, who have no blood relation. Using qiyas, the prohibition is extended from blood sisters to foster-sisters. The author further notes that this prohibition is not based on severing the womb (since there is no womb between foster-siblings) but is established by the analogy. Later, he mentions that a hadith will come to refute the statement from al-Mabsut. The passage concludes by stating that combining sisters in ownership (as concubines) without sexual intercourse is permissible, as the prohibition is only for sexual access.

Key Terms
الجمع بين الأختين (al-jam' bayna al-ukhtayn): Having two sisters simultaneously as wives or as concubines
الرضاعة (al-rada'ah): Fosterage; the suckling relationship that creates mahram bonds
محارم (mahārim): Relatives whom one is permanently forbidden to marry
ملك يمين (milk al-yamin): Right hand possession; concubinage through ownership of a female slave

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of combining two sisters is established by Quran and Hadith, and extends to foster-sisters via qiyas; ownership without intercourse is permissible.

Marrying the Sister of One's Slave-Girl: Validity and Prohibition
Ruling on marrying the sister of a slave-concubine

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that the marriage is valid and explain the condition for permissible intercourse.

Core Idea
Marriage to the sister of one's concubine is valid, but intercourse with either is haram until the concubine is disposed of.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a nuanced case in marriage law: a man owns a slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse, then marries her sister. The commentator clarifies two key points: the validity of the marriage contract and the temporary prohibition of intercourse. He also responds to an objection that the marriage should be invalid due to combining sisters legally.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling components
The passage states two things: (1) the marriage to the sister is valid, and (2) he may not have intercourse with either woman until the slave-girl is sold. Distinguish between the contract's validity and the prohibition of intercourse.
2
Follow the objection and response
An objection is raised: since the married woman is 'legally a concubine' (because lineage is established by contract alone), he would be combining two sisters in intercourse, which should invalidate the marriage. The response: this legal combination is not inevitable because he can remove it by disposing of the slave-girl.
Understanding the concept of 'legal concubine' (موطوءة حكماً) is key.
3
Note the condition
The prohibition only applies if the slave-girl has been actually used for intercourse (muwatu'ah). If she has not, the ruling differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فلو تزوج أخت أمته الموطوءة لم يطأ واحدة منهما حتى يبيعها بيان لشيئين : أحدهما صحة نكاح الأخت مع كون أختها موطوءة له بملك اليمين لصدوره من أهله مضافاً إلى محله وأورد عليه أن المنكوحة موطوءة حكماً باعترافكم فيصير بالنكاح جامعاً وطئاً حكماً وهو باطل، وجوابه أن لزوم الجمع بينهما وطئاً حكماً ليس بلازم لأن بيده إزالته فلا يضر بالصحة ويمنع من الوطء بعدها لقيامه إذا ذاك . أطلق في الأخت زوجة الابن ولا بنتها ولا زوجة الربيب ولا زوجة الراب . قوله : (وسيأتي حديث يرده) أي يأتي عند قول المصنف وبين امرأتين» حديث يرد ما ذكره في المبسوط من أن حرمة الجمع ليس لقطيعة الرحم والجواب عن قوله فإنه ليس بين الرضيعين رحم الخ» قوله : (وأورد عليه أن المنكوحة موطوءة حكماً) أي بدليل ثبوت نسب ولدها بمجرد العقد حتى لو نكح مشرقي مغربية ثبت نسب أولادها منه قوله : فيصير) بالنكاح جامعاً وطئاً) أما في المنكوحة
His statement: (If he marries the sister of his slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse, he may not have intercourse with either of them until he sells her) is an explanation of two things: one, the validity of marrying the sister even though her sister is his concubine, because the contract issues from one who is qualified and applies to its proper place. An objection is raised that the married woman is legally a concubine by your admission, so by the marriage he becomes a person combining sexual intercourse legally, which is invalid. The answer: the necessity of combining them legally is not necessary because he can remove it, so it does not harm validity, but it prevents intercourse after the marriage due to its existence at that time. He made it absolute in the sister, the wife of the son, nor her daughter, nor the wife of the stepson, nor the wife of the father-in-law. His statement: (And a hadith will come to refute it) meaning at the author's statement 'and between two women' a hadith will refute what was mentioned in al-Mabsut that the prohibition of combining is not due to cutting the womb. And the response to his statement 'there is no womb between the two foster-siblings' etc. His statement: (And it was objected that the married woman is legally a concubine) meaning by the evidence that the lineage of her child is established merely by the contract, so if an Easterner marries a Westerner, the lineage of their children is established from him. His statement: (so by the marriage he becomes combining sexual intercourse) as for the married woman...
Source pages p. 168

Commentary
This passage deals with the specific case where a man owns a slave-girl with whom he has had intercourse, and then marries her sister. The ruling: the marriage is valid, but he cannot have intercourse with either the slave-girl or the newly married sister until he disposes of the slave-girl (e.g., by selling her). The text addresses an objection: that since the married woman is 'legally' considered a concubine (because lineage is established by mere contract), he would be combining both in intercourse legally, which should invalidate the marriage. The answer is that this legal combination is not inevitable because he can remove it by selling the slave-girl, so the marriage is valid, but he is prevented from intercourse while the basis of prohibition remains. The passage also includes a reference to a hadith that will come to refute a point from al-Mabsut regarding the reason for prohibition.

Key Terms
أمة موطوءة (amah muwatu'ah): Slave-girl with whom her master has had sexual intercourse
الجمع بينهما وطئاً (al-jam' baynahuma wat'an): Combining both sisters in sexual access, whether actual or legal

Marrying Two Sisters Unknowingly: Invalidity and Separation
Commentary on the ruling and its detailed sub-rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying two sisters in separate contracts without knowing the first, and distinguish the positions on whether the separation is talaq or faskh.

Core Idea
Marrying two sisters in ignorance requires separation from both; the separation is talaq in the mufta bihi view.

When a man marries two sisters in two contracts and cannot recall which came first, both marriages are invalid and he must separate from both women. This lesson unpacks the detailed ruling from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, including the obligation of separation, the means to resolve the prohibition, and the scholarly debate over whether the separation counts as talaq or faskh. Understanding this ruling clarifies how the Hanafi school balances the prohibition of combining sisters with the legal effects of marriage contracts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the ruling
State the specific scenario: a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts and does not know which was first. The ruling is that both marriages are batil (invalid) and he must separate from both women.
The base text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq is quoted: 'ولو تزوج أختين في عقدين ولم يدر الأول فرق بينه وبينهما'.
2
Identify the proof and its basis
The prohibition of combining sisters is based on the hadith 'لا يجمع بين المرأة وعمتها' (a man may not combine a woman and her aunt). This is extended to sisters by qiyas. The commentary expands on the evidence for the ruling.
The hadith is ahad (zanni al-thubut) but its meaning (dalala) is clear and prohibitive.
3
Trace the dispute: talaq vs. faskh
Al-Marghinani in Fath al-Qadir states the apparent view is talaq, meaning the separation counts as one divorce from each wife. Some Hanafis and other schools hold it is faskh (annulment) with no divorce count. Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) regarding 'iddah and remarriage.
The tarjih in the Hanafi school is that it is talaq, as relied upon by later authorities.
4
Analyze the conditions for resolution
After separation, the man may have intercourse with one sister only after making the other unlawful to him by a cause (e.g., selling a slave with whom he had intercourse, or valid marriage). The commentary details invalid causes like invalid marriage or sale without possession.
The key distinction is between actual combining (by intercourse) and legal combining (by contract).
5
Apply to edge cases
Note exceptions: if one sister is already married to another or in 'iddah, the marriage of the other is valid. Also, if the man owns two slave sisters, he may have intercourse with one but then must not combine them. The passage provides many subsidiary rulings.
These edge cases follow from the principle of avoiding definite combining.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو تزوج أختين في عقدين ولم يدر الأول فرق بينه وبينهما ولهما نصف المهر وبين المتزوجة فشمل ما إذا كانت أمة أو حرة ثانيهما حرمة وطء واحدة منهما حتى يبيعها لأنه لو جامع المنكوحة يصير جامعاً بينهما وطئاً حقيقة، ولو جامع المملوكة يصير جامعاً بينهما حقيقة وحكماً. والمراد بالبيع أنه يحرم الموطوءة على نفسه بسبب من الأسباب فحينئذ يطأ المنكوحة لعدم الجمع كالبيع كلاً أو بعضاً والتزويج الصحيح والهبة مع التسليم والإعتاق كلاً أو بعضاً والكتابة، وأما التزويج الفاسد فلا عبرة به إلا إذا دخل بها فتحرم حينئذ الموطوءة لوجوب العدة عليها فتحل حينئذ المنكوحة. وكذا المراد بالتزويج في المختصر النكاح الصحيح فلو تزوج الأخت نكاحاً فاسداً لم تحرم عليه أمته الموطوءة إلا إذا دخل بالمنكوحة فحينئذ تحرم الموطوءة لوجود الجمع بينهما حقيقة ولا يؤثر الإحرام والحيض والنفاس والصوم، وكذا الرهن والإجارة والتدبير لأن فرجها لا يحرم بهذه الأسباب . كذا في التبيين من فصل الاستبراء، وإذا عادت الموطوءة إلى ملكه بعد الإخراج، سواء كان بفسخ أو بشراء جديد لم يحل وطء واحدة منهما حتى يحرم الأمة على نفسه بسبب كما كان أولاً. وأطلق في الأمة فشمل أم الولد كما في غاية البيان، وقيد بكونها موطوءة لأنه لو لم يكن وطئها جاز له وطء المنكوحة لأن المرقوقة ليست بموطوءة حكماً فلم يصر جامعاً بينهما وطأ لا حقيقة ولا حكماً. وأشار المصنف إلى أنه لو تزوج جارية ولم يطأها . ملك أختها فليس له أن يطأ المشتراة لأن المنكوحة موطوءة حكماً، وإلى أنه لو ملك أختين له أن يطأ إحداهما فإذا وطئ إحداهما ليس له وطء الأخرى بعد ذلك، وإلى أنه لو ملك جارية فوطئها ثم ملك أختها كان له أن يطأ الأولى وليس له وطء الأخرى ما لم يحرم فرج الأولى على نفسه، ولو وطئها أثم ثم لا يحل له وطء واحدة منهما حتى يحرم الأخرى بسبب .

الثبوت فله أن يدعي نكح من شاء بعينه منهن تمسكاً بما كان متيقناً ولم يثبت هنا نكاح واحدة منهما بعينها، فدعواه حينئذ تمسك بما لم يتحقق ثبوت. ومعنى فرق بينه وبينهما أنه يفترض عليها مفارقتهما، ولو علم القاضي بذلك وجب عليه أن يفرق بينهما دفعاً للمعصية بقدر الإمكان كما في المحيط، ولم يذكر في المختصر أن هذا التفريق طلاق أو فسخ . وفي فتح القدير : والظاهر أنه طلاق حتى ينقص من طلاق كل منهما طلقة لو تزوجها بعد ذلك فإن وقع قبل الدخول فله أن يتزوج أيتهما شاء للحال أو بعده فليس له التزوج بواحدة منهما حتى تنقضي عدتهما، وإن انقضت عدة إحداهما دون الأخرى فله تزوج التي لم تنقض عدتها دون الأخرى كيلا يصير جامعاً، وإن وقع بعده بإحداهما فله أن يتزوجها في الحال دون الأخرى فإن عدتها تمنع من تزوج أختها ا وقيد بكونه تزوجهما في عقدين إذ لو كانا في عقد واحد بطلا يقيناً، وقيده في المحيط بأن لا تكون إحداهما مشغولة بنكاح الغير أو عدته، فإن كانت كذلك صح نكاح الفارغة لعدم تحقق الجمع بينهما كما لو تزوجت امرأة زوجين في عقد واحد وأحدهما متزوج بأربع نسوة فإنها تكون زوجة للآخر لأنه لم يتحقق الجمع بين رجلين إذا كانت هي لا تحل لأحدهما ا هـ.
If he marries two sisters in two contracts and he does not know which was first, he must separate from both and they are entitled to half the dowry each. The married one (the second) includes whether she is a slave or free. Then it is forbidden to have intercourse with either of them until he sells [one of them]. Because if he has intercourse with the married one, he becomes actually combining between them by intercourse. If he has intercourse with the owned one, he becomes combining between them actually and legally. What is meant by 'sell' is that he makes the one with whom intercourse occurred forbidden to himself by some cause, then he may have intercourse with the married one due to absence of combining. This includes sale in whole or part, valid marriage, gift with delivery, manumission in whole or part, and kitaba. As for invalid marriage, it is not considered unless he entered her, then the one with whom intercourse occurred becomes forbidden due to the 'iddah becoming obligatory, so the married one becomes permissible. Similarly, what is meant by 'marriage' in the Mukhtasar is valid marriage. If he marries a sister with an invalid marriage, his own slave with whom he had intercourse is not forbidden unless he entered the married one, then the slave becomes forbidden due to actual combining. Ihram, menstruation, postpartum bleeding, and fasting have no effect, similarly pledge, lease, and tadbir because her private part is not forbidden by these causes. As stated in al-Tabyin from the chapter of istibra'. If the slave with whom intercourse occurred returns to his ownership after being removed, whether by annulment or new purchase, it is not permissible to have intercourse with either of them until he makes the slave forbidden to himself by a cause as before. He used 'slave' generally, including umm walad as in Ghayat al-Bayan, and restricted it to being one with whom intercourse occurred because if he had not had intercourse with her, it would be permissible for him to have intercourse with the married one, because the owned one is not considered as one with whom intercourse occurred legally, so he is not combining between them by intercourse actually or legally. The author indicated that if he marries a slave girl and does not have intercourse with her, then owns her sister, he may not have intercourse with the purchased one because the married one is considered as one with whom intercourse occurred legally. And that if he owns two sisters, he may have intercourse with one of them, and if he has intercourse with one, he may not have intercourse with the other thereafter. And that if he owns a slave girl and has intercourse with her, then owns her sister, he may have intercourse with the first but not the other until he makes the first's private part forbidden to himself, and if he has intercourse [with the second] he sins, then it is not permissible to have intercourse with either of them until he makes the other forbidden by a cause.
Until
His saying: (If he marries two sisters in two contracts and does not know the first, he must separate from both) because the marriage of one of them is definitely invalid, and there is no way to specify because there is no priority, nor to execute with ignorance because there is no benefit or due to harm, so separation is determined. A distinction was demanded between this and the case where he divorces one of his wives specifically and forgets her, where he is ordered to specify and does not separate from all. The answer: there it is possible, here it is not, because their marriages were certain.
Al-Nahr
As we said, and in the case of the slave, the ruling of the first intercourse remains, so istibra' is recommended for her when desiring to sell her. Similarly his saying: (What is meant by 'sell' is that he makes the slave with whom intercourse occurred forbidden to himself by a cause etc.) He said in al-Nahr: I have not seen in their statements what if he sold her in a corrupt sale or gifted similarly and she was taken into possession, the apparent is that intercourse with the married one becomes permissible. I say: This is based on the corrupt gift giving ownership with possession, which is the fatwa position as in al-Durar and others, contrary to what is corrected in al-Imadiyya.
His saying: (As for invalid marriage, it is not considered) al-Ramli said: i.e., if a man marries a woman with an invalid marriage, it is not considered unless the husband entered her, then her sister that the master married becomes permissible. What is meant by entry is intercourse, because mere seclusion in invalid marriage does not necessitate 'iddah. His saying: (nor to execution) i.e., execution of a marriage of an unspecified woman, as evidence by his saying 'with ignorance', and accordingly specification necessitates execution and not vice versa. His saying: (he has)
Establishment, so he may claim the marriage of whichever he wants specifically from them, adhering to what was certain. But here the marriage of one specific is not established, so his claim then is adherence to something whose establishment is not confirmed. The meaning of 'separate between him and them' is that she must separate from them, and if the judge knows that, he must separate them to prevent sin as much as possible as in al-Muhit. It is not mentioned in al-Mukhtasar whether this separation is talaq or faskh. In Fath al-Qadir: The apparent is that it is talaq, so a divorce is counted from each if he marries her subsequently. If it occurs before entering, he may marry whichever he wishes immediately; if after, he may not marry either until their 'iddah expires. If the 'iddah of one expires but not the other, he may marry the one whose 'iddah has not expired but not the other, to avoid combining. If it occurs after entering with one, he may marry that one immediately but not the other, because her 'iddah prevents marrying her sister. And it is restricted to being in two contracts, for if they were in one contract they would be definitely invalid. And he restricted in al-Muhit that one of them should not be occupied by another's marriage or her 'iddah; if so, the marriage of the free one is valid due to lack of verified combining, as if a woman marries two husbands in one contract and one of them is married to four women, then she is the wife of the other because there is no verified combining of two men when she is not permissible to either. End.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding a man who marries two sisters in two separate contracts without knowing which marriage contract was concluded first. The ruling states that both marriages are invalid and he must separate from both women, with each entitled to half of the specified dowry (mahr) if the husband had not consummated the marriage; if consummation occurred, the full dowry is due. The commentary elaborates on several subsidiary rules: it explains the means by which the man can make one sister lawful for intercourse after the separation, such as selling the slave with whom he had intercourse or marrying her off validly, and clarifies that invalid sales or gifts do not suffice unless delivery gives ownership (according to the fatwa position). It distinguishes between different types of prohibition: actual combining (by intercourse) and legal combining (by marriage or valid contract). The commentary also discusses the situation when the man owns one slave sister and marries the other, and the rules regarding intercourse with owned slaves. It addresses the nature of the separation (talaq vs. faskh), noting that the preferred view in Fath al-Qadir is that it is talaq, which counts toward the three divorces. The passage further considers the condition that the two marriages must be in separate contracts; if in one contract, both are definitely invalid. Also, if one sister was already married to another person or in her 'iddah, the marriage of the other is valid because there is no actual combining. The commentary follows the author's order, explaining each phrase of the base text.

Key Terms
أختين (ukhtayn): Two sisters (full or half) whom a man marries or owns simultaneously.
عقدين (aqdayn): Two separate marriage contracts, as opposed to a single contract combining both.
الجمع (al-jam'): Combining two women in marriage or ownership that are prohibited to be together, such as sisters.
الموطوءة (al-mawtu'a): The slave woman or wife with whom the man has had sexual intercourse.
البيع (al-bay'): Sale (the means by which the man makes the prohibited sister unlawful to himself).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the mufta bihi ruling on the nature of separation when a man marries two sisters in two contracts without knowing the first?
A) It is faskh (annulment) with no divorce counted.
B) It is talaq (divorce) counting as one divorce from each wife if consummated.
C) It is a revocable divorce that does not reduce the remaining divorces.
D) The separation is not required if the man divorces one immediately.

Key Takeaway
Marrying two sisters in separate contracts without knowledge of the order invalidates both, requiring separation (ruled as talaq) and half-dowry, with the prohibition resolved only by making one sister unlawful through a valid cause.

Marrying Two Sisters in Two Contracts with Unknown Priority
Ruling on two contracts with unknown priority and nature of judicial separation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling that both marriages are valid when priority is unknown, and explain why the compulsory separation is considered talaq rather than faskh.

Core Idea
Marrying two sisters in separate contracts with unknown priority: both marriages are valid, but separation is required and counts as talaq.

When a man marries two sisters in two separate contracts but cannot determine which contract came first, the Hanafi school does not automatically invalidate the marriages. Instead, the marriages are considered valid because there was no certain prohibition at the time of each contract. However, the judge must order separation (tafriq) to end the ongoing sin of living with both. A key question arises: is this separation considered talaq (divorce) or faskh (annulment)? This lesson explores the reasoning and the preferred view.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal issue
The man has married two sisters in two separate contracts, but the priority is unknown. Determine the status of each marriage under Hanafi fiqh.
2
Determine the initial ruling
Both marriages are valid (sahih) because there is no certainty of prohibited combination at the time of each contract. The marriages are not automatically void.
3
Understand the role of the judge
Once the judge learns of the situation, he must order separation (tafriq) to remove the ongoing sin of living with two sisters simultaneously.
The judge's duty is to prevent sin (دفع المعصية) as much as possible.
4
Analyze the nature of tafriq: talaq or faskh?
Al-Mukhtasar left this ambiguous. Fath al-Qadir clarifies that the apparent view is talaq, because it reduces the number of divorces available to the man (ينقص من طلاق كل منهما طلقة).
The practical implication: if talaq, the man's right to remarry after 'iddah is subject to the number of divorces; if faskh, no such reduction.
5
Apply the consequences
If separation occurs before consummation, he may immediately marry whichever sister he chooses. If after consummation, he must wait until both 'iddahs expire. If only one expires, he may only marry the one whose 'iddah is ongoing, to avoid recombining.
Also, if one sister is already married to another or in 'iddah, the marriage to the free one is valid without need for separation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الثبوت فله أن يدعي نكاح من شاء بعينه منهن تمسكاً بما كان متيقناً ولم يثبت هنا نكاح واحدة منهما بعينها، فدعواه حينئذ تمسك بما لم يتحقق ثبوت. ومعنى فرق بينه وبينهما أنه يفترض عليها مفارقتهما، ولو علم القاضي بذلك وجب عليه أن يفرق بينهما دفعاً للمعصية بقدر الإمكان كما في المحيط، ولم يذكر في المختصر أن هذا التفريق طلاق أو فسخ . وفي فتح القدير : والظاهر أنه طلاق حتى ينقص من طلاق كل منهما طلقة لو تزوجها بعد ذلك فإن وقع قبل الدخول فله أن يتزوج أيتهما شاء للحال أو بعده فليس له التزوج بواحدة منهما حتى تنقضي عدتهما، وإن انقضت عدة إحداهما دون الأخرى فله تزوج التي لم تنقض عدتها دون الأخرى كيلا يصير جامعاً، وإن وقع بعده بإحداهما فله أن يتزوجها في الحال دون الأخرى فإن عدتها تمنع من تزوج أختها. وقيد بكونه تزوجهما في عقدين إذ لو كانا في عقد واحد بطلا يقيناً، وقيده في المحيط بأن لا تكون إحداهما مشغولة بنكاح الغير أو عدته، فإن كانت كذلك صح نكاح الفارغة لعدم تحقق الجمع بينهما كما لو تزوجت امرأة زوجين في عقد واحد وأحدهما متزوج بأربع نسوة فإنها تكون زوجة للآخر لأنه لم يتحقق الجمع بين رجلين إذا كانت هي لا تحل لأحدهما ا هـ. فإذا كانا في عقد واحد فرق بينها وبينهما أيضاً فإن كان قبل الدخول فلا مهر لهما ولا عدة عليهما، وإن دخل بهما وجب لكل الأقل من المسمى ومن مهر المثل كما هو حكم النكاح الفاسد وعليهما العدة وقيده بعدم علم العقد الأول إذ لو علم فهو الصحيح والثاني باطل وله وطء الأولى إلا أن يطأ الثانية فتحرم الأولى إلى انقضاء عدة الثانية كما لو وطئ أخت امرأته بشبهة حيث تحرم امرأته ما لم تنقض عدة ذات الشبهة. وفي الدراية عن الكامل: لو زنى بإحدى الأختين لا يقرب الأخرى حتى تحيض الأخرى حيضة. واستشكله في فتح القدير ولم يبينه ووجهه أنه لا اعتبار لماء الزاني ولذا لو زنت امرأة رجل لم تحرم عليه وجاز له وطؤها عقب الزنا. ولو قال المصنف «ولو تزوج أختين في عقدين معاً أو لم يدر الأول فرق بينه وبينهما لكان أفود لما في الذخيرة معزياً
The established fact, so he may claim the marriage of whichever he wishes, specifically among them, holding fast to what was certain, and here the marriage of none of them is established specifically. Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling from Kanz al-Daqa'iq regarding marrying two sisters. The author first discusses the case of two contracts with unknown priority, explaining the principle of claiming which sister he married based on certainty. He then details the obligation of separation by the judge and the debate whether it constitutes talaq or faskh. The relied-upon opinion (mufta bihi) is that it is talaq, so it reduces the number of divorces. He then explains the consequences for remarriage based on timing. Then he transitions to the case of a single contract, which is batil, and gives further conditions regarding mahr and 'iddah. He also addresses the case of zina with one sister and the disagreement with Ibn Wahban's view.

Key Terms
تفريق (tafriq): Compulsory separation decreed by the judge between a man and his wives due to prohibited combination (e.g., marrying two sisters).
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage that lacks a necessary condition but not entirely void; it requires separation and has mahr if consummated. (Not directly used in this lesson's primary scenario, but relevant for the single contract case.)

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is faskh, annulling both marriages.
B) It is talaq, reducing one divorce from each wife.
C) It is a judicial nullification without effect on divorce counts.
D) It is considered a single talaq for both wives together.

Key Takeaway
Marrying two sisters in two separate contracts with unknown priority results in valid marriages, but the judge must separate them; the separation is considered talaq and reduces the divorce count for each wife.

Marrying Two Sisters in a Single Contract and Consequences
Ruling on single contract for two sisters and related consequences with mahr, 'iddah, and shubha

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state that marrying two sisters in a single contract is batil, and explain the rulings on mahr, 'iddah, and the effect of consummation.

Core Idea
Marrying two sisters in one contract is batil (void) from the start, with no mahr before consummation and only the lesser of specified and proper mahr after.

Whereas marrying two sisters in two separate contracts leads to valid marriages requiring separation, marrying them in a single contract is fundamentally different. The Hanafi school rules this contract as batil (void) ab initio. This lesson examines the consequences: no mahr or 'iddah if before consummation, and the lesser of the specified dower and proper dower if consummated. It also explores the analogy with cases of shubha and zina.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two scenarios
When a man marries two sisters in a single contract, it is batil (void) from the beginning, unlike two contracts where marriages are sahih.
The Arabic says: 'وقيد بكونه تزوجهما في عقدين إذ لو كانا في عقد واحد بطلا يقيناً'.
2
Determine the consequence before consummation
If the judge separates them before consummation, there is no mahr (dower) for either wife and no 'iddah (waiting period) upon them.
Because the contract is void, it produces no legal effects.
3
Determine the consequence after consummation
If he consummated with both, each wife is entitled to the lesser of the specified mahr and the proper mahr (mahr al-mithl). They must observe 'iddah.
This is the same as the ruling for a fasid (invalid) marriage in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Consider the effect of knowledge
If the man knew the first marriage was valid, he cannot claim ignorance; the first is valid and the second is batil. He may have intercourse with the first only.
If he has intercourse with the second, the first becomes prohibited until the second's 'iddah expires, analogous to shubha with a wife's sister.
5
Analyze the analogy with zina
The text discusses a view from al-Kamil regarding zina with one sister and its effect on approaching the other. Fath al-Qadir finds this problematic, noting that zina does not create prohibition.
This shows the limits of analogy: shubha creates prohibition, but zina does not.

Key Terms
نكاح فاسد (nikah fasid): An invalid marriage that lacks a necessary condition but not entirely void; it requires separation and has mahr if consummated.
شبهة (shubha): A semblance of right or legality that arises from an honest mistake, affecting rulings like prohibition of marriage or hadd punishment.

Checkpoint
A man marries two sisters in a single contract and consummates. What mahr is owed to each sister?
A) The full specified mahr.

Marrying two sisters in one contract is batil; if consummated, each wife receives the lesser of specified and proper mahr and must observe 'iddah.

intermediate
10 min
Claiming Marriage to a Specific Sister and the Effect of Zina on Marriage
Critiques the claim of marriage and discusses zina's effect.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why a mere claim of marriage to a specific sister is insufficient in Hanafi law and distinguish the Hanafi positions on whether zina affects a husband's right to intercourse.

Core Idea
Mere claim cannot establish marriage in private matters; zina does not create prohibition according to the majority Hanafis.

This lesson examines two related issues in Hanafi fiqh: first, the difficulty of a man claiming he intended to marry a specific sister when he married two sisters in separate unknown contracts; second, the dispute over whether a wife's act of zina prohibits her husband from intercourse. The passage shows the careful reasoning of Hanafi jurists in protecting certainty while acknowledging the caution preferred by Imam Muhammad.

Guided Path
1
Identify the problem of claim
Understand why a mere claim of marriage to a specific sister, without evidence or preference, is problematic because investigation into private matters (taharrī) is prohibited in such cases.
The text contrasts this with a case where the marriage was previously established with certainty.
2
Analyze the ruling on mahr when both marriages are batil
When both marriages are definitely void due to combining sisters, no mahr is owed because the marriages are invalid ab initio.
This is derived from the principle that a batil contract does not entitle the wife to mahr.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute on zina and istibra'
Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that a wife who commits zina does not become prohibited to her husband, and no istibra' is required. Imam Muhammad recommends istibra' (waiting for one menses) but does not consider it obligatory.
The relied-upon view is that of the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), though some later scholars like Ibn Wahban proposed a different opinion.
4
Evaluate the critique of Ibn Wahban's position
The commentator in al-Nahr and others deem Ibn Wahban's view weak, as it contradicts the stronger transmission from the early imams and the principle that the sperm of the zani has no legal effect.
This critique reflects the Hanafi emphasis on textual evidence over speculative caution.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أن يدعي نكاح من شاء بعينه منهن الخ أقول : إن أريد أن له الدعوى من غير ترجيح فمشكل لأن التحري في الفروج ممنوع وإن أريد مع المرجح فلا فرق وينبغي أن لا يحل له ديانة بمجرد الدعوى. كذا في الرمز ا هـ. لكن في قوله فلا فرق نظر لأن نكاح من ادعى نكاحها كان قبل ثابتاً بيقين بخلافه في مسألتنا قوله : (وإن وقع بعده) أي بعد الدخول قوله : (بطلاً يقيناً) أي للجمع بين الأختين فلا يستحقان شيئاً من المهر اهـ .درر قوله : ( ووجهه أنه لا اعتبار لماء الزاني) قال في النهر : يشكل عليه ما في نظم ابن وهبان ولو زنت امرأة حرمت على زوجها حتى تحيض وتطهر. وعزاه في الشرح إلى النتف معللاً باحتمال علوقها من الزنا فلا يسقي ماؤه زرع غيره إلا أن يدعي ضعفه ، وسيأتي أن الموطوءة بزنا يحل وطؤها بالنكاح من غير استبراء عندهما. وقال محمد: لا أحب أن يطأها غير أن يستبرئها ا هـ. قلت: وممن صرح بضعف ما ذكره ابن وهبان تلميذ المؤلف في منحه وتبعه
That he may claim the marriage of whichever he wishes specifically among them, etc. I say: If what is meant is that he has the claim without preference, it is problematic because investigation into private parts is prohibited. If what is meant is with preference, then there is no difference. And he should not be allowed religiously by mere claim. Thus in al-Ramz. End. But in his saying 'no difference' there is consideration, because the marriage he claimed was previously established with certainty, unlike our issue. His statement: (And if it occurred after) meaning after consummation. His statement: (Definitely batil) meaning due to combining two sisters, so they deserve nothing of the mahr. End. Durar. His statement: (And its reasoning is that the sperm of the zani is not considered). He said in al-Nahr: It is problematic what is in the versification of Ibn Wahban: 'If a woman commits zina, she becomes prohibited to her husband until she menstruates and becomes pure.' He attributed it in the commentary to al-Nutaf, reasoning by the possibility of pregnancy from zina, so his sperm should not irrigate another's crop unless its weakness is claimed. It will come that a woman subject to zina is permissible for intercourse in marriage without istibra' according to them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Muhammad said: I do not like that he has intercourse with her unless he performs istibra'. End. I say: Among those who explicitly stated the weakness of what Ibn Wahban mentioned is the student of the author in his Manhah, and he followed that.

Commentary
This passage is a critical refinement, commenting on the previous ruling. It first addresses the issue of a man claiming marriage to a specific sister from the two sisters he had married in two contracts of unknown priority. The commentator (likely the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq) raises the problem: allowing the man to simply claim which sister he intended is not straightforward because investigation of private parts is prohibited. If he claims with some preference, it may be acceptable, but he should not be allowed simply by claim. The passage then discusses the mahr when the marriage is batil due to combining sisters. Finally, it addresses a reported statement from al-Nahr criticizing Ibn Wahban's view that a woman who commits zina becomes prohibited to her husband until she menstruates. The Hanafi position is that she does not become prohibited; Imam Muhammad prefers istibra' but not prohibition.

Key Terms
تحري (taharrī): Investigation or seeking to determine; here, investigating which sister he married, which is discouraged in matters of private parts.
استبراء (istibra'): A period of waiting to ensure the womb is free from pregnancy; here, after zina before intercourse in marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She becomes permanently prohibited.
B) She becomes temporarily prohibited until she menstruates.
C) She remains permissible, no prohibition.
D) He must divorce her.

Key Takeaway
Mere claim of marriage to a specific sister is insufficient, and zina does not create prohibition according to the majority Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), though Imam Muhammad recommended caution through istibra'.

Simultaneous Marriage Proposals to Sisters: Hanafi Rulings
Rulings on simultaneous proposals to sisters via agents and direct offers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for each of the four scenarios involving simultaneous marriage offers to two sisters and explain why combination in one half of the contract invalidates the marriage.

Core Idea
Combination in one half of the marriage contract invalidates both in the case of two sisters.

Marriage to two sisters simultaneously is prohibited by explicit Quranic text. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies how that prohibition applies when the proposal or acceptance occurs via agents, unauthorized intermediaries, or the sisters themselves. Understanding whose 'side' the combination occurs on is critical to determining the validity of the contract.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four scenarios
The passage gives four distinct scenarios: (1) two appointed agents marry two sisters simultaneously, (2) two unauthorized (fuduli) agents do the same, (3) two sisters simultaneously offer themselves to one man who accepts one, (4) the man simultaneously proposes to both sisters.
Each scenario tests whether the combination of two sisters in the marriage transaction occurs from the man's side (invalid) or the sisters' side (may be valid).
2
Locate the operative principle
The key principle is that a 'combination in one half of the contract' (shatr al-'aqd) is sufficient to invalidate the marriage. The half here is the proposal (ijab) or acceptance (qabul).
The passage explicitly states: 'combination in one half of the contract causes invalidity, just as combination in both halves of the contract.'
3
Apply the principle to each scenario
For scenario (1): The agents' statements are attributed to the principal, so the combination occurs in the proposal from the man's side → both batil. For scenario (2): Since agents are fuduli, their acts are suspended; the man can validate one. For (3): The combination is from the sisters' side (each speaks individually), and the man accepts only one → valid. For (4): The combination is from the man's proposal side → batil if even one sister accepts.
4
Note the qiyas illustration
The passage extends the ruling to a case of five women: if a man says 'I have married all of you' and one accepts, the combination in the proposal invalidates all. This is a qiyas jali (clear analogy) proving the principle.
The illa (effective cause) is the combination of multiple women in a single proposal from the man's side.
5
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference between appointed agents and fuduli agents: in the former, both contracts are automatically batil; in the latter, the man may choose one upon ratification. This nuance affects how a mufti advises in real cases.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح فصل في المحرمات امرأتين أية فرضت ذكر حرم النكاح والزنا واللمس والنظر بشهوة يوجب حرمة. إلى الجامع : لو وكل رجل رجلاً أن يزوجه امرأة ووكل رجلاً آخر بمثل ذلك فزوجه كل واحد منهما امرأة وهما أختان من الرضاع ووقع العقدان منهما معاً فهما باطلان لأن عبارة الوكيل في باب النكاح منقولة إلى الموكل، فإذا خرج الكلامان معاً صار كأن الموكل خاطبهما بالنكاح، فلو لم يوكلهما وإنما كانا فضوليين ووقعا معاً فللزوج أن يجيز نكاح إحداهما، ولو خرج إيجاب الأختين معاً بأن قالت كل واحدة منهما لرجل واحد زوجت نفسي منك بكذا وخرج الكلام منهما معاً فقبل الزوج نكاح إحداهما فهو جائز لعدم الجمع من الزوج، وأما من الأختين فلأن كل واحدة زوجت نفسها على حدة ولا ولاية لإحداهما على صاحبتها حتى ينقل كلام كل إلى الأخرى ولو بدأ الزوج فقال تزوجتكما كل واحدة منكما بألف فقالت إحداهما رضيت وأبت الأخرى فنكاحها باطل لوجود الجمع في الخطاب بينهما في إحدى شطري العقد وأنه كافٍ للفساد، ألا ترى أن رجلاً لو قال لخمس نسوة قد تزوجتكن على ألف فقالت إحداهما رضيت لا يجوز نكاحهن لوجود الجمع من جانب الزوج فعلم به أن الجمع في إحدى شطري العقد يوجب الفساد كالجمع في شطري العقد ا هـ . اختصار منه . مع بعض
Book of Marriage, Section on Prohibited [Women]: Two sisters, whichever is assumed, mention of prohibition of marriage, zina, touch, and look with desire establishes prohibition. To the comprehensive: If a man appoints a man to marry a woman for him, and appoints another man similarly, and each marries him a woman, and they are two sisters through rada', and the two contracts occur simultaneously, then they are both batil because the statement of the agent in the chapter of marriage is transferred to the principal. When the two statements occur simultaneously, it becomes as if the principal addressed both with marriage. If he did not appoint them and they were Fuduli [unauthorized agents] and it occurred simultaneously, then the husband may validate the marriage of one of them. And if the offer of the two sisters occurs together, such that each of them says to one man 'I married myself to you for such and such' and the speech comes from both simultaneously, and the husband accepts the marriage of one of them, it is valid because there is no combination from the husband. As for the two sisters, each married herself separately, and neither has guardianship over the other such that the speech of each is transferred to the other. If the husband begins and says 'I married both of you, each of you for a thousand', and one of them says 'I accept' and the other refuses, then her marriage is batil due to the existence of combination in the address between them in one half of the contract, and that is sufficient for invalidity. Do you not see that if a man says to five women 'I have married all of you for a thousand' and one of them says 'I accept', their marriage is not valid due to the presence of combination from the husband's side? So it is known that combination in one half of the contract causes invalidity, just as combination in both halves of the contract. End. Abbreviation from it. With some.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage begins with a brief rule: two sisters, by whatever assumption, marriage, zina, touch, or look with desire establishes prohibition. Then it presents a detailed case from the work Jami' al-Kabir or similar: if a man appoints two separate agents to marry two women, and the agents simultaneously perform the marriage contracts for two sisters (by rada'), both contracts are batil because the agents' statements are attributed to the principal, so it is as if the principal himself proposed to both sisters simultaneously, which is prohibited. However, if the agents were unauthorized (Fuduli), the husband can validate one. Next, if two sisters themselves each simultaneously offer themselves in marriage to one man (without agents), and the man accepts one, it is valid because the combination is from the sisters' side, not the man's, and each sister has no authority over the other. But if the man initiates by saying 'I marry both of you', and only one accepts, the contract is invalid due to the combination in the proposal. The author illustrates with the example of a man addressing five women; the marriage is invalid if the combination is from his side.

Key Terms
وكيل (wakil): An agent appointed to perform a marriage contract on behalf of another (the principal).
فضولي (Fuduli): An unauthorized agent who performs a contract without prior appointment; the contract is suspended until ratification.
شطر العقد (shatr al-'aqd): One half of a contract; here, the proposal (ijab) or acceptance (qabul). Combination in one half can invalidate the contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the passage, what is the ruling if two fuduli (unauthorized) agents simultaneously marry two sisters to the same man?
A) Both marriages are batil immediately
B) The man may validate one marriage upon ratification
C) The first marriage is valid, the second is batil
D) The man must reject both and can later remarry

Key Takeaway
Combination in one half of the marriage contract (the proposal) from the man's side invalidates the marriage, but combination from the sisters' side does not if only one is accepted.
