Simultaneous Marriage of Sisters: Invalidity and Mahr
Explains rulings when two agents marry two sisters simultaneously

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on simultaneous marriage of two sisters via agents and apply the four conditions for half mahr entitlement.

Core Idea
Simultaneous marriage of two sisters is invalid; half mahr is due to both under four conditions resolving unknown priority.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses a nuanced scenario: when two agents marry two foster-sisters to the same man at exactly the same moment. The ruling explores invalidity due to prohibited combination and then delves into the mahr obligation when priority cannot be determined. You will learn the conditions under which half mahr is awarded and how intra-Hanafi differences are resolved.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary scenario and ruling
Two agents each marry a woman to the same man; the women are foster-sisters and both contracts occur simultaneously. Both marriages are invalid.
The agent's speech is attributed to the principal, making it as if the principal married both simultaneously.
2
Understand why invalidity occurs
In Hanafi law, the agent's statement in marriage is transferred to the principal. Simultaneous marriage to two sisters constitutes prohibited combination (jam').
If the agents were volunteers (fudaliyyun), the husband may ratify one marriage.
3
Examine the mahr problem
Since one marriage was valid (the first) but which is unknown, half mahr is awarded to both as a solution based on istihsan.
This is restricted by four conditions derived from the later scholars.
4
Analyze the four conditions
(1) Mahr specified; (2) Mahr equal; (3) Separation before consummation; (4) Both women claim to be first without evidence.
If all conditions are met, each gets half her specified mahr. If mahr amounts differ, the ruling is debated.
5
Evaluate intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held nothing is due (unknown recipient), Muhammad held full mahr for both (admission of validity). The mufta bihi is half mahr with the four conditions.
The fourth condition (from al-Hinduwani) refutes Abu Yusuf's objection.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب النكاح فصل في المحرمات امرأتين أية فرضت ذكر حرم النكاح والزنا واللمس والنظر بشهوة يوجب حرمة إلى الجامع : لو وكل رجل رجلاً أن يزوجه امرأة ووكل رجلاً آخر بمثل ذلك فزوجه كل واحد منهما امرأة وهما أختان من الرضاع ووقع العقدان منهما معاً فهما باطلان لأن عبارة الوكيل في باب النكاح منقولة إلى الموكل، فإذا خرج الكلامان معاً صار كأن الموكل خاطبهما بالنكاح، فلو لم يوكلهما وإنما كانا فضوليين ووقعا معاً فللزوج أن يجيز نكاح إحداهما، ولو خرج إيجاب الأختين معاً بأن قالت كل واحدة منهما لرجل واحد زوجت نفسي منك بكذا وخرج الكلام منهما معاً فقبل الزوج نكاح إحداهما فهو جائز لعدم الجمع من الزوج، وأما من الأختين فلأن كل واحدة زوجت نفسها على حدة ولا ولاية لإحداهما على صاحبتها حتى ينقل كلام كل إلى الأخرى ولو بدأ الزوج فقال تزوجتكما كل واحدة منكما بألف فقالت إحداهما رضيت وأبت الأخرى فنكاحها باطل لوجود الجمع في الخطاب بينهما في إحدى شطري العقد وأنه كافٍ للفساد، ألا ترى أن رجلاً لو قال لخمس نسوة قد تزوجتكن على ألف فقالت إحداهما رضيت لا يجوز نكاحهن لوجود الجمع من جانب الزوج فعلم به أن الجمع في إحدى شطري العقد يوجب الفساد كالجمع في شطري العقد ا هـ . اختصار منه . مع بعض قوله : (ولهما نصف المهر لأنه وجب للأولى منهما وانعدمت الأولوية للجهل بالأولية فيصرف إليهما أطلقه وهو مقيد بأربعة قيود كما قالوا الأول أن يكون المهر مسمى في العقد فلو لم يكن مسمى وجبت متعة واحدة لهما بدل نصف المهر وتركه اعتماداً على ما يصرح به في باب المهر الثاني أن يكون مهراهما متساويين إذ لو كانا مختلفين يقضى لكل واحدة منهما بربع مهرها ولا حاجة إلى التقييد به لأنه لم يقل ولهما نصف المهر على السواء الحصكفي قوله : (لما في الذخيرة إلى قوله فهما باطلان قال في النهر : كيف يتم هذا مع قوله ولهما نصف المهر» وهذا لأن الباطل لا مهر فيه . هـ. قوله : (إذ لو كانا مختلفين يقضى لكل واحدة منهما بربع (مهرها كذا ذكره الزيلعي والكمال وفي شرح الشيخ إسماعيل عن اليعقوبية. وهذا مخالف لما في الكافي والكفاية وهو أن لهما الأقل من نصفي المهرين لأن فيه يقيناً ! . قال الشيخ إسماعيل والاحتياط القضاء بما في الكافي والكفاية لأن الأول مطروق باحتمال فكان قضاء بمحتمل اهـ. وقد فصل في الدرر فقال : وإن اختلفا أي مسماهما فإن علما فلكل ربع مهرها وإلا فلكل واحدة نصف أقل المسميين. واعترضه محشوه بأن قوله «فلكل صوابه فلهما وبأن ما ذكره من التفصيل لم يوجد في شيء من الكتب. قال الشيخ إسماعيل : والظاهر أن المصنف أراد أن يوفق بين ما وقع في التبيين وبين ما وقع في الكافي وغيره بأن الأول فيما إذا كان ما سمى لكل واحدة منهما بعينها معلوماً كالخمسمائة لفاطمة والألف لزاهدة، والثاني فيما إذا لم يكن معلوماً كذلك بأن يعلم أنه لواحدة منهما خمسمائة وللأخرى ألف إلا نه نسي تعيين كل منهما لكن سياق ما في الكافي والكفاية لا يؤدي انحصاره وفيما أشير إلى حمله عليه، ولذا قيل : لو حمل على اختلاف الرواية لكان أولى قوله : ( مع أنه مشكل) قال الرملي : أي إيجاب مهر كامل لكل واحدة منهما. وقوله ويجيب حمله أي حمل القضاء بمهر كامل وعقر كامل . حتى يرد عليه ذلك . الثالث أن يكون قبل الدخول إذ لو كانت الفرقة بعد الدخول يجب لكل واحدة المهر كاملاً لأنه استقر بالدخول فلا يسقط منه شيء، ولا حاجة إلى التقييد به لأن نصف المهر حكم الفرقة قبل الدخول مع أنه مشكل بل إذا كان بعد الدخول فإنه يقضى بمهر كامل وعقر كامل، ويجب حمله على ما إذا اتحد المسمى لهما قدراً وجنساً، أما إذا اختلفا فيتعذر إيجاب عقر إذ ليست إحداهما أولى بجعلها ذات العقد من الأخرى لأنه فرع الحكم بأنها الموطوءة في النكاح الفاسد الرابع أن تدعي كل واحدة منهما أنها الأولى ولا بينة لهما، أما إذا قالتا لا ندري أي النكاحين أول لا يقضى لهما بشيء لأن المقضى له مجهول وهو يمنع صحة القضاء كمن قال لرجلين لأحدهما على ألف لا يقضى لأحدهما بشيء إلا أن يصطلحا بأن يتفقا على أخذ نصف المهر منه فيقضى لهما ،به وهذا القيد الرابع زاده أبو جعفر الهندواني، فظاهر الهداية تضعيفه لكنه حسن يندفع به قول أبي يوسف أنه لا شيء لهما لجهالة المقضى له، والمروي عن محمد من وجوب مهل كامل لهما لإقرار الزوج بجواز نكاح إحداهما أبعد لاستلزامه إيجاب الشيء مع تحقق عدم لزومه فإن إيجاب كماله حكم الموت أو الدخول حقيقة أو حكماً وهو مفقود. وفي التبيين وكل ما ذكرنا من الأحكام بين الأختين فهو الحكم بين كل من لا يجوز جمعه من المحارم .
Book of Marriage, Chapter on Prohibitions. 'Two women, whichever is mentioned first, [the ruling is that] sexual intercourse, touching, and looking with desire are prohibited and cause prohibition.' Up to al-Jami': If a man appoints one agent to marry a woman and appoints another similarly, and each marries a woman and they are two foster-sisters, and the two contracts occur simultaneously, then both are invalid because the agent's statement in marriage is transferred to the principal. So if the two statements emerge together, it is as if the principal addressed both in marriage. If he did not appoint them but they were volunteers (fudaliyyun) and the marriages occur simultaneously, then the husband has the option to ratify the marriage of one of them. If the offer from the two sisters occurs simultaneously, each saying to one man 'I married myself to you for such amount' and the speech emerges together, and the husband accepts the marriage of one of them, it is valid because there is no combination (jam') from the husband. As for the sisters, each married herself separately, and neither has authority over the other such that each's speech is transferred to the other. If the husband began by saying 'I have married both of you, each for a thousand,' and one said 'I accept' and the other refused, then her marriage is invalid because of the presence of combination in the address between them in one part of the contract (shatr al-'aqd), and that is sufficient for invalidity. Do you not see that if a man said to five women 'I have married all of you for one thousand' and one of them accepted, it is not permissible for them to be married because of combination from the husband's side? Thus it is known that combination in one part of the contract causes invalidity like combination in both parts. End summary from it. With some of his statement: (And for them is half the dower because it is obligatory for the first of them, but priority is non-existent due to ignorance of which was first, so it is paid to both). This is unrestricted, but it is restricted by four conditions as they said: first, that the dower be specified in the contract; if not specified, then one single gift (mut'a) is obligatory for both instead of half the dower, and he omitted this relying on what is clarified in the chapter on dower. Second, that their two dowers be equal; if they differ, then each is awarded one quarter of her dower, and there is no need to restrict it because he did not say 'and for them is half the dower equally'. Al-Haskafi's statement: (Due to what is in al-Dhakhirah up to his saying 'they are both invalid'. In al-Nahr: How is this consistent with his saying 'and for them is half the dower'? This is because an invalid marriage has no dower.) His statement: (If they were different, each is awarded one quarter of her dower). This is mentioned by al-Zayla'i and al-Kamal, and in Sharh al-Shaykh Isma'il from al-Ya'qubiyyah. This contradicts what is in al-Kafi and al-Kifayah, which is that they receive the lesser of the two halves of the two dowers because that contains certainty. Al-Shaykh Isma'il said: The cautious approach is to judge according to what is in al-Kafi and al-Kifayah because the first is open to probability, so it is a ruling based on conjecture. He concluded. And al-Durar detailed it: If the two specified dowers differ and they are known, then each has one quarter of her dower; otherwise each has half of the smaller of the two specified dowers. Its annotator objected: his saying 'each' should be 'both', and what he mentioned of detail is not found in any book. Al-Shaykh Isma'il said: It appears that the author intended to reconcile between what is in al-Tabyin and what is in al-Kafi and others: the first case is when what is specified for each is known individually, like 500 for Fatima and 1000 for Zahida; the second is when it is not known in that way, but it is known that one of them has 500 and the other 1000 but the assignment is forgotten. However, the context of al-Kafi and al-Kifayah does not restrict to that, and it was indicated to be interpreted that way. Hence it was said: if it were interpreted as a difference in transmission (riwaya) that would be better. His statement: (while it is problematic) al-Ramli said: meaning obligation of full mahr for each of them. And his saying 'it must be interpreted' means interpreting the ruling of full mahr and full 'aqr (compensation). Until that is objected to. Third: that it be before consummation; if separation occurs after consummation, each is entitled to full mahr because it is established by consummation and nothing is dropped. There is no need for this restriction because half mahr is the ruling for separation before consummation, though it is problematic. Rather, if after consummation, full mahr and full 'aqr are ruled. This must be interpreted as when the specified dower for both is the same in amount and type; if they differ, it is impossible to impose 'aqr because neither is more entitled to be considered the one with the valid contract, since that is based on the ruling that she is the one who was actually penetrated in the invalid marriage. Fourth: that each of them claims that she was the first and neither has evidence. If they say 'we do not know which marriage was first', nothing is awarded to them because the recipient is unknown, which prevents the validity of judgment, just as if someone said to two men 'one of them owes me a thousand', nothing is awarded to either unless they settle by agreeing to take half the dower from him, then it is awarded to them. This fourth condition was added by Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani; the apparent of al-Hidayah is to weaken it, but it is good, by which the statement of Abu Yusuf is refuted that nothing is due to them due to the unknown recipient. And the narrated from Muhammad of the obligation of full mahr for both due to the husband's admission that the marriage of one of them is valid is more remote because it necessitates obligating something while its non-necessity is realized; imposing its full amount is a ruling of death or consummation, actual or legal, which is absent. And in al-Tabyin: All the rulings we mentioned between two sisters are the ruling between all those whose simultaneous marriage is not permitted.
Source pages p. 171

Commentary
This passage from the chapter on prohibited women in marriage addresses complex scenarios when two related women (sisters) are married simultaneously to one man. The first part discusses the case of two agents appointed by the same man, each marrying a different woman, and the two women are foster-sisters. If both marriages occur at the same time, both are invalid because the agent's speech is attributed to the principal, so it is as if the principal himself married both simultaneously. If the agents were not appointed but acted voluntarily (fudaliyyun), the husband may ratify one of the marriages. When the women themselves offer marriage simultaneously, the husband's acceptance of one is valid because the combination (jam') occurs from the women's side, not his. However, if the husband speaks first and combines them in his offer, and only one accepts, the marriage is invalid due to combination in one part of the contract, which is sufficient for nullity. The second part addresses the entitlement to half mahr when two sisters are married in invalid contracts and it is unknown which marriage occurred first, so priority is undetermined. The author states that half mahr is given to both, but this is restricted by four conditions: (1) the mahr must be specified in the contract; if not, a single gift (mut'a) is substituted; (2) the two mahrs must be equal; if they differ, each receives one quarter of her own mahr according to the dominant view, though there is debate—some say they get the lesser of the two halves; (3) separation must occur before consummation; after consummation, full mahr is due; (4) each woman must claim she was first without evidence; if both admit ignorance, nothing is awarded. The fourth condition is attributed to Abu Ja'far al-Hinduwani and is accepted despite some weakness reported in al-Hidayah, as it resolves the objection of Abu Yusuf that nothing is due due to unknown recipient. The passage concludes that these rulings apply not only to sisters but to all women whose simultaneous marriage is prohibited (mahram).

Key Terms
وكيل (wakīl): An agent appointed by the principal to perform the marriage contract.
فضولي (fudūlī): A person who acts without prior authorization; an unauthorized volunteer.
جمع (jamʿ): Combining two women in marriage who are prohibited to be married together, e.g., two sisters.
شطر العقد (shaṭr al-ʿaqd): One part (half) of a marriage contract, either the offer (ijab) or the acceptance (qabul).
مهر (mahr): The obligatory dower paid by the husband to the wife upon marriage or by contract stipulation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if two agents simultaneously marry two foster-sisters to the same man, what is the ruling on the marriages?
A) Both marriages are valid if the mahr is paid.
B) Both marriages are invalid because of prohibited combination.
C) Only the marriage of the first agent is valid.
D) The husband can choose which one to keep.

Key Takeaway
Simultaneous marriage of two sisters is invalid in all forms, and when priority is unknown, half mahr under four conditions is the relied-upon ruling.

Prohibition of Combining Two Mahram Women in Marriage
States the rule and hadith prohibiting marrying two related women (e.g., aunt and niece)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining two mahram women in marriage, identify the hadith proof, and explain the underlying illa (prevention of cutting family ties).

Core Idea
Marrying two mahram women simultaneously is haram to prevent severing family ties.

This lesson addresses a specific prohibition in nikah: marrying two women who are mahram to each other at the same time. The ruling is based on authentic hadith and extended by analogy to all such relationships. Understanding the underlying cause (illa) is key to applying the rule correctly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
What is the act being ruled upon? Combining (jamʿ) two women in marriage who are mahram to each other. The ruling is haram (unconditional prohibition).
Mahram here means if one were male, marriage between them would be impermissible.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith from Muslim: 'Do not marry a woman on her paternal aunt, nor on her maternal aunt, nor on her brother's daughter, nor on her sister's daughter.' This is a well-known hadith (mashhur).
This hadith is ahad but mutawatir in meaning, so it is qatʿi al-thubut.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit prohibition of those specific relationships indicates the ruling. The underlying cause (illa) is preventing severance of family ties (qatiʿa al-rahim), as narrated in the hadith of Abu Dawud and al-Tabarani.
The illa is derived from the texts: 'for fear of cutting ties'.
4
Extend the ruling by qiyas
Since the illa is preserving kinship, the prohibition extends to all relationships where the women are mahram to each other, such as mother-daughter (by blood or fosterage).
This extension is consistent across the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبين امرأتين أية فرضت ذكر أحرم (النكاح أي حرم الجمع بين امرأتين إذا كانتا بحيث لو قدرت إحداهما ذكراً حرم النكاح بينهما أيتهما كانت المقدرة ذكراً كالجمع بين المرأة وعمتها والمرأة وخالتها، والجمع بين الأم والبنت نسباً أو رضاعاً لحديث مسلم تنكح المرأة على عمتها ولا على خالتها ولا على ابنة أخيها ولا على ابنة أختها» (۱) وهذا مشهور يجوز تخصيص عموم الكتاب وأحل لكم ما وراء ذلكم [النساء : ٢٤] به ويدل على اعتبار الأصل المذكور ما ثبت في الحديث برواية الطبراني وهو قوله «فإنكم إذا فعلتم ذلك قطعتم أرحامكم ولرواية أبي داود: نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تنكح المرأة على قرابتها مخافة القطيعة. فأوجب تعدي الحكم المذكور إلى كل قرابة يفرض وصلها وهو ما تضمنه الأصل
His statement: 'And between two women, whichever is mentioned first, He prohibited marriage' i.e., He prohibited combining two women in marriage when they are such that if one of them were supposed to be male, marriage between them would be prohibited, whichever is supposed to be male. Examples: combining a woman with her paternal aunt, a woman with her maternal aunt, and combining a mother and daughter by lineage or fosterage, due to the hadith of Muslim: 'Do not marry a woman on [i.e., simultaneously with] her paternal aunt, nor on her maternal aunt, nor on her brother's daughter, nor on her sister's daughter.' This is a well-known hadith; it is permissible to specify the general Quranic verse 'And lawful to you are all beyond that' (Quran 4:24) with it. And it indicates the consideration of the mentioned principle what is established in the hadith narrated by al-Tabarani: 'For if you do that, you cut your wombs' and by Abu Dawud: 'The Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, prohibited marrying a woman on [simultaneously with] her relative for fear of cutting ties.' So it necessitated extending the mentioned ruling to every relationship whose connection is supposed, which is what the principle implies.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage clarifies the prohibition of marrying two women who are mahram to each other. The author explains that the ruling applies between any two women such that if one were male, marriage between them would be prohibited. Common examples include a woman and her paternal aunt, maternal aunt, mother and daughter, and similar relationships by lineage or fosterage. The primary proof is the hadith from Muslim: 'Do not marry a woman simultaneously with her paternal aunt, nor with her maternal aunt, nor with her brother's daughter, nor with her sister's daughter.' This hadith specifies the general permission in Quran 4:24. The underlying rationale, as indicated in the hadith of al-Tabarani and Abu Dawud, is to prevent cutting off family ties (qati'a al-arham). Since the principle is based on the preservation of kinship, the prohibition extends to all female relatives who would be mahram if one were male, not just those explicitly mentioned in the hadith. The commentary emphasizes that the ruling is derived from the Sunnah (hadith) and that it can specify the general Quranic text because it is a well-known authentic hadith. The purpose is to maintain harmonious family relations by avoiding conflicts that could arise from such marriages.

Key Terms
جمع (jamʿ): Combining two women in marriage who are related by blood or fosterage such that they would be mahram if one were male.
عمّة (ʿamma): Paternal aunt, i.e., the sister of a man's father.
خالة (khāla): Maternal aunt, i.e., the sister of a man's mother.
قرابة (qarāba): Kinship or blood relationship; also includes fosterage (rida'a) in the context of mahram.
قطيعة الرحم (qatīʿa al-rahim): Severance of family ties, which is forbidden in Islam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the underlying reason (illa) for prohibiting the simultaneous marriage of a woman and her paternal aunt?
A) To prevent concentration of wealth within a family.
B) To prevent cutting off family ties (qati'a al-rahim).
C) Because the aunt is considered like a mother.
D) Because it is specified in the Quran without further reasoning.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prohibits combining two mahram women in marriage based on a clear hadith and the illa of preventing severance of family ties, extending the ruling to all similar relationships.

Conditions for Mahr when Two Women Claim Marriage
Conditions for judgment when two women claim marriage with no evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four conditions under which a Hanafi judge rules on mahr when two women each claim a valid marriage without evidence, and identify the operative position (mufta bihi) among the views of Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and al-Hindawani.

Core Idea
If neither woman can prove priority, nothing is adjudged; they must reconcile.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, a commentary on Kanz al-Daqaiq, addresses a nuanced scenario: two women each claim to be the wife in a valid marriage or a corrupt marriage with no evidence. The author, Zayn al-Din ibn Nujaym, presents the conditions for a judge to award mahr, including the requirement that both women claim to be the first wife. He also discusses an intra-Hanafi dispute among Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and the later addition by Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani. Understanding this ruling helps navigate cases of disputed marriage where textual proof is absent.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core scenario
Two women each assert that they are the wife of the same man through a valid marriage (nikah sahih) and that the other's marriage is corrupt (nikah fasid). No evidence supports either claim.
The man is absent or deceased; the judge must decide on mahr.
2
List the necessary conditions for judgment
From the passage, extract the conditions: (1) separation before consummation, (2) the specified mahr for both women is identical in amount and type, (3) each claims to be the first wife, (4) they have no evidence. If these hold, each gets half the mahr and half the 'uqr.
If after consummation, full mahr and full 'uqr are due, provided the mahr amounts match.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Yusuf held that nothing is due because the recipient is unknown. Muhammad held that full mahr is due to both based on the husband's admission. Abu Hanifa's view (as transmitted) gives half before consummation. Al-Hindawani added the fourth condition to resolve the conflict.
The author supports al-Hindawani's condition, calling it 'hasan' (good).
4
Apply the rule when priority is unknown
If both women say 'we do not know which marriage was first', the judge adjudges nothing until they reconcile. This is because the recipient is unknown, analogous to a man owing a debt to one of two persons but not knowing which.
The analogy (qiyas) with debt clarifies the principle.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حتى يرد عليه ذلك . الثالث أن يكون قبل الدخول إذ لو كانت الفرقة بعد الدخول يجب لكل واحدة المهر كاملاً لأنه استقر بالدخول فلا يسقط منه شيء، ولا حاجة إلى التقييد به لأن نصف المهر حكم الفرقة قبل الدخول مع أنه مشكل بل إذا كان بعد الدخول فإنه يقضى بمهر كامل وعقر كامل، ويجب حمله على ما إذا اتحد المسمى لهما قدراً وجنساً، أما إذا اختلفا فيتعذر إيجاب عقر إذ ليست إحداهما أولى بجعلها ذات العقد من الأخرى لأنه فرع الحكم بأنها الموطوءة في النكاح الفاسد الرابع أن تدعي كل واحدة منهما أنها الأولى ولا بينة لهما، أما إذا قالتا لا ندري أي النكاحين أول لا يقضى لهما بشيء لأن المقضى له مجهول وهو يمنع صحة القضاء كمن قال لرجلين لأحدهما على ألف لا يقضى لأحدهما بشيء إلا أن يصطلحا بأن يتفقا على أخذ نصف المهر منه فيقضى لهما به وهذا القيد الرابع زاده أبو جعفر الهندواني، فظاهر الهداية تضعيفه لكنه حسن يندفع به قول أبي يوسف أنه لا شيء لهما لجهالة المقضى له، والمروي عن محمد من وجوب مهر كامل لهما لإقرار الزوج بجواز نكاح إحداهما أبعد لاستلزامه إيجاب الشيء مع تحقق عدم لزومه فإن إيجاب كماله حكم الموت أو الدخول حقيقة أو حكماً وهو مفقود. وفي التبيين وكل ما ذكرنا من الأحكام بين الأختين فهو الحكم بين كل من لا يجوز جمعه من المحارم .
until he responds to that. Third: that it be before consummation, because if separation occurred after consummation, each one deserves the full mahr because it is established by consummation, so nothing is dropped. There is no need to restrict it because half mahr is the ruling of separation before consummation, although it is problematic. Rather, if it is after consummation, then a full mahr and full 'uqr are adjudged. It must be interpreted as when the specified mahr for both is the same in amount and type. However, if they differ, it is impossible to impose a 'uqr because neither is more deserving to be considered the one with the valid marriage contract over the other, because it is subordinate to the ruling that she is the one who was sexually enjoyed in the corrupt marriage. Fourth: that each of the two women claims that she is the first (in time) and there is no evidence for them. However, if they say 'We do not know which marriage was first', nothing is adjudged to them because the recipient is unknown, which prevents the validity of judgment, just as if a man says to two men 'One of them has a thousand against me', nothing is adjudged to either unless they reconcile by agreeing to take half the mahr from him, then it is adjudged to them. This fourth restriction was added by Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani. The apparent of al-Hidayah weakens it, but it is good, and with it the statement of Abu Yusuf is refuted that they deserve nothing due to the ignorance of the recipient. What is narrated from Muhammad regarding the obligation of a full mahr for both is based on the husband's acknowledgment of the permissibility of marrying one of them, but this is far-fetched because it entails obligating something while its necessity is not established, for obligating its full amount is a ruling of death or consummation actually or legally, which is absent. And in al-Tabyin: all that we mentioned of rulings between two sisters is the ruling between everyone whose combination is not permissible from among the prohibited relatives.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling regarding two women who each claim to be the wife in a valid marriage versus a corrupt marriage. The author explains conditions: the separation must be before consummation for half-mahr; if after, full mahr is due. Additionally, both must claim to be first without evidence; if uncertain, nothing is adjudged. The fourth condition added by Abu Ja'far al-Hindawani is accepted, refuting Abu Yusuf's view that they get nothing. Muhammad's view (full mahr) is considered weak. The ruling generalizes to all prohibited combinations.

Key Terms
المهر (al-mahr): The dower paid to the wife in a valid marriage; here discussed in context of disputed marriages.
العقر (al-'uqr): The analogous payment in a corrupt marriage (nikah fasid), equivalent to mahr.
النكاح الفاسد (al-nikah al-fasid): A marriage that is defective in a necessary condition but not inherently invalid; differs from batil.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) They each get half the mahr.
B) They each get a full mahr.

D) They must provide witnesses.

Key Takeaway
When two women claim marriage without evidence and do not know priority, the Hanafi judge adjudges nothing until they agree on a settlement.

The Prohibition of Combining Close Female Relatives in Marriage
Ruling and proof for combining close relatives

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on combining a woman with her close female relative, cite the hadith proof, and apply the hypothetical test (if one were male).

Core Idea
Combining a woman with her paternal aunt, maternal aunt, or niece is haram because it would become incest if one were male.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational ruling that prohibits marrying a woman while simultaneously being married to her close relative. The Hanafi school derives this from explicit hadith and applies it through a clever hypothetical test: if one of the two women were a man, would marriage between them be prohibited? If yes, combining them is haram.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The prohibited act is combining two women in marriage such that if one were male, marriage between them would be forbidden. The ruling is haram.
2
Locate the dalil
The primary proof is the hadith narrated by Muslim: 'Do not marry a woman on her paternal aunt, nor on her maternal aunt, nor on her brother's daughter, nor on her sister's daughter.'
Also narrated by Abu Dawud with the cause mention.
3
Apply the hypothetical test
Consider the two women: if one were a man, would they be allowed to marry? If not, then combining them is prohibited.
E.g., a woman and her paternal aunt: if the aunt were a man, she would be a mahram, so prohibition.
4
Understand the specification of the Quranic general text
The Quran says 'and lawful to you are all others besides these' (al-Nisa 4:24). The hadith specifies that certain combinations are excluded from this general permission.
This is a case of takhsis al-amm, permissible because the hadith is sahih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبين امرأتين أية فرضت ذكر أحرم (النكاح أي حرم الجمع بين امرأتين إذا كانتا بحيث لو قدرت إحداهما ذكراً حرم النكاح بينهما أيتهما كانت المقدرة ذكراً كالجمع بين المرأة وعمتها والمرأة وخالتها، والجمع بين الأم والبنت نسباً أو رضاعاً لحديث مسلم تنكح المرأة على عمتها ولا على خالتها ولا على ابنة أخيها ولا على ابنة أختها» (۱) وهذا مشهور يجوز تخصيص عموم الكتاب وأحل لكم ما وراء ذلكم [النساء : ٢٤] به ويدل على اعتبار الأصل المذكور ما ثبت في الحديث برواية الطبراني وهو قوله «فإنكم إذا فعلتم ذلك قطعتم أرحامكم ولرواية أبي داود: نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تنكح المرأة على قرابتها مخافة القطيعة. فأوجب تعدي الحكم المذكور إلى كل قرابة يفرض وصلها وهو ما تضمنه الأصل المذكور فيتخرج عليه حرمة الجمع بين عمتين وخالتين وذلك أن يتزوج كل من الرجلين أم الآخر فيولد لكل منهما بنت فتكون كل من البنتين عمة للأخرى، أو يتزوج كل من رجلين بنت الآخر ويولد لهما بنتان فكل من البنتين خالة للأخرى. وبما قرر علم أن العلة خوف القطيعة، وظهر به ضعف ما قدمناه عن المبسوط من أن العلة ليس ذلك إذ لا قرابة بين الأختين رضاعاً. وجوابه أن حرمة الجمع بينهما للحديث يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب. والمراد بالحرمة في قوله حرم النكاح الحرمة المؤبدة، أما المؤقتة فلا تمنع ولذا لو تزوج أمة ثم سيدتها فإنه يجوز كما في الجامع والزيادات لأنها حرمة مؤقتة بزوال ملك اليمين. وقيل: لا يجوز تزوج السيدة عليها نظراً إلى مطلق الحرمة كما في القنية. وقيد بقوله «أية فرضت» لأنه لو جاز نكاح إحداهما على تقدير مثل المرأة وبنت زوجها أو امرأة ابنها فإنه يجوز الجمع بينهما عند الأئمة الأربعة، وقد جمع عبد الله بن جعفر بين زوجة علي وبنته ولم ينكر عليه أحد . وبيانه أنه لو فرضت بنت الزوج ذكراً بأن كان ابن الزوج لم يجز له أن يتزوج بها لأنها موطوءة أبيه ، ولو فرضت المرأة ذكراً لجاز له أن يتزوج ببنت الزوج لأنها بنت رجل أجنبي، وكذلك بين المرأة وامرأة ابنها فإن المرأة لو فرضت ذكراً لحرم عليه التزوج بامرأة ابنه، ولو فرضت امرأة الابن ذكراً لجاز له التزوج بالمرأة لأنه أجنبي عنها. قالوا: ولا بأس أن يتزوج الرجل امرأة ويتزوج ابنه أمها أو بنتها لأنه لا مانع وقد تزوج محمد بن الحنفية امرأة وزوج ابنه بنتها .
His saying: (And between two women, whichever you consider as a male, the marriage is prohibited.) That is, it is forbidden to combine two women in marriage if they are such that if one of them were considered a male, marriage between them would be forbidden, regardless of which one is considered the male. Examples: combining a woman with her paternal aunt, a woman with her maternal aunt, and combining a mother with her daughter, whether by lineage or suckling, due to the hadith of Muslim: 'Do not marry a woman on her paternal aunt, nor on her maternal aunt, nor on her brother's daughter, nor on her sister's daughter.' This is well-known, and it is permissible to specify the general meaning of the verse 'and lawful to you are all others besides these' [4:24] with it. It indicates the consideration of the aforementioned principle what is established in the hadith narrated by al-Tabarani, which is his saying: 'For if you do that, you cut off your wombs.' And according to Abu Dawud's narration: 'The Messenger of Allah forbade that a woman be married on her close relative out of fear of cutting off ties.' So it obliged extending the mentioned ruling to every kinship that is presumed to be connected, which is what the aforementioned principle entails. From this branch the prohibition of combining two paternal aunts and two maternal aunts: that is, if each of two men marries the other's mother, and each gives birth to a daughter, then each of the two daughters becomes a paternal aunt of the other; or if each of two men marries the other's daughter, and each gives birth to two daughters, then each of the two daughters becomes a maternal aunt of the other. And from what was established it is known that the cause is fear of cutting off ties, and it becomes apparent the weakness of what we presented from al-Mabsut that the cause is not that, since there is no kinship between two sisters through suckling. The response is that the prohibition of combining them is due to the hadith 'what is prohibited through suckling is what is prohibited through lineage.' And the meaning of 'hurma' in his saying 'marriage is prohibited' is the permanent prohibition. As for temporary prohibition, it does not prevent, so if a man marries a slave girl and then [marries] her female owner, it is permissible, as in al-Jami' and al-Ziyadat, because it is a temporary prohibition that ends with the removal of ownership. It is said: it is not permissible to marry the female owner over her, considering the absolute prohibition, as in al-Qunyah. And it is restricted by his saying 'whichever you consider as a male', because if it were permissible to marry one of them hypothetically, like a woman and her husband's daughter or his son's wife, then combining them is permissible according to the four imams. Abdullah ibn Ja'far combined between Ali's wife and his daughter, and no one objected to him. Its explanation: if the husband's daughter were considered a male (i.e., a son), he would not be permitted to marry her because she is the one who was sexually enjoyed by his father; if the woman were considered a male, he would be permitted to marry the husband's daughter because she is the daughter of an unrelated man. Similarly, between a woman and her son's wife: if the woman were considered a male, he would be prohibited from marrying his son's wife; if the son's wife were considered a male, he would be permitted to marry the woman because he is unrelated to her. They said: there is no harm if a man marries a woman and his son marries her mother or her daughter, because there is no obstacle. Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah married a woman and married his son to her daughter.
Source pages p. 172

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the rule forbidding combining two close female relatives in marriage, based on explicit hadith. The key is the hypothetical test: if one woman were male, would marriage between her and the other be prohibited? If yes, combining them is haram. The cause is fear of severing family ties. The rule applies only to permanent prohibition; temporary prohibitions (like slavery) are excluded. The condition 'ayyata faradta' clarifies that if the hypothetical marriage would be permissible, then combining is permissible (e.g., step-relations). Examples from practice (Abdullah ibn Ja'far) support the permissibility of certain combinations.

Key Terms
العمة (al-'ammah): Paternal aunt; combining a woman with her paternal aunt is prohibited.
الخالة (al-khala): Maternal aunt; similarly prohibited.
الحرمة المؤبدة (al-hurma al-mu'abbada): Permanent prohibition; the type of prohibition that creates a permanent bar to marriage.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith quoted, which combination is explicitly prohibited?
A) A woman and her cousin.
B) A woman and her paternal aunt.
C) A woman and her stepmother.
D) A woman and her grandmother.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of combining a woman with her close relative is based on the hypothetical test derived from hadith, and it applies to all mahram relatives.

Extensions, Cause, and Exceptions to the Prohibition
Extension and cause of the prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the cause (خوف القطيعة) for the prohibition, use qiyas to extend the ruling to all close relatives, and identify the exceptions (temporary prohibitions and permissible combinations).

Core Idea
The prohibition extends via qiyas to any relative whose connection would be severed, but it does not apply to temporary prohibitions or cases where the hypothetical marriage would be permissible.

Building on the previous lesson, we now explore the rationale behind the prohibition and how the Hanafi jurists extended it to all close relatives through legal analogy (qiyas). We also examine the exceptions that confirm the rule, such as the permissibility of combining step-relatives and the distinction between permanent and temporary prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the cause (ʿilla)
The hadith from Abu Dawud indicates the cause is 'fear of cutting off family ties' (خوف القطيعة). This is the effective cause for the ruling.
The author refutes al-Mabsut's claim that there is no such cause for suckling relatives, citing the principle that suckling creates the same prohibitions as lineage.
2
Apply qiyas to extend the ruling
From the explicit cases (paternal aunt, maternal aunt, etc.) the jurists extend the prohibition to any relative whose ties would be severed. Example: combining two women who become each other's 'amma through a marriage chain.
The new cases are derived via qiyas based on the same cause.
3
Recognize the condition of permanent prohibition
The prohibition applies only to permanent prohibitions (حرمة مؤبدة). Temporary prohibitions (e.g., a slave girl and her owner) do not trigger the rule.
There is a difference of opinion: some later texts rule that it is not permissible to combine a slave girl and her owner due to the temporary prohibition.
4
Apply the hypothetical test in reverse
If the hypothetical marriage would be permissible (e.g., a woman and her stepdaughter), then combining is allowed. Examples from the Companion Abdullah ibn Ja'far support this.
This confirms that the rule is based on the test, not a blanket prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : ( وبين امرأتين أية فرضت ذكر أحرم (النكاح أي حرم الجمع بين امرأتين إذا كانتا بحيث لو قدرت إحداهما ذكراً حرم النكاح بينهما أيتهما كانت المقدرة ذكراً كالجمع بين المرأة وعمتها والمرأة وخالتها، والجمع بين الأم والبنت نسباً أو رضاعاً لحديث مسلم تنكح المرأة على عمتها ولا على خالتها ولا على ابنة أخيها ولا على ابنة أختها» (۱) وهذا مشهور يجوز تخصيص عموم الكتاب وأحل لكم ما وراء ذلكم [النساء : ٢٤] به ويدل على اعتبار الأصل المذكور ما ثبت في الحديث برواية الطبراني وهو قوله «فإنكم إذا فعلتم ذلك قطعتم أرحامكم ولرواية أبي داود: نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أن تنكح المرأة على قرابتها مخافة القطيعة. فأوجب تعدي الحكم المذكور إلى كل قرابة يفرض وصلها وهو ما تضمنه الأصل المذكور فيتخرج عليه حرمة الجمع بين عمتين وخالتين وذلك أن يتزوج كل من الرجلين أم الآخر فيولد لكل منهما بنت فتكون كل من البنتين عمة للأخرى، أو يتزوج كل من رجلين بنت الآخر ويولد لهما بنتان فكل من البنتين خالة للأخرى. وبما قرر علم أن العلة خوف القطيعة، وظهر به ضعف ما قدمناه عن المبسوط من أن العلة ليس ذلك إذ لا قرابة بين الأختين رضاعاً. وجوابه أن حرمة الجمع بينهما للحديث يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب. والمراد بالحرمة في قوله حرم النكاح الحرمة المؤبدة، أما المؤقتة فلا تمنع ولذا لو تزوج أمة ثم سيدتها فإنه يجوز كما في الجامع والزيادات لأنها حرمة مؤقتة بزوال ملك اليمين. وقيل: لا يجوز تزوج السيدة عليها نظراً إلى مطلق الحرمة كما في القنية. وقيد بقوله «أية فرضت» لأنه لو جاز نكاح إحداهما على تقدير مثل المرأة وبنت زوجها أو امرأة ابنها فإنه يجوز الجمع بينهما عند الأئمة الأربعة، وقد جمع عبد الله بن جعفر بين زوجة علي وبنته ولم ينكر عليه أحد . وبيانه أنه لو فرضت بنت الزوج ذكراً بأن كان ابن الزوج لم يجز له أن يتزوج بها لأنها موطوءة أبيه ، ولو فرضت المرأة ذكراً لجاز له أن يتزوج ببنت الزوج لأنها بنت رجل أجنبي، وكذلك بين المرأة وامرأة ابنها فإن المرأة لو فرضت ذكراً لحرم عليه التزوج بامرأة ابنه، ولو فرضت امرأة الابن ذكراً لجاز له التزوج بالمرأة لأنه أجنبي عنها. قالوا: ولا بأس أن يتزوج الرجل امرأة ويتزوج ابنه أمها أو بنتها لأنه لا مانع وقد تزوج محمد بن الحنفية امرأة وزوج ابنه بنتها .

Does Zina Establish Mushahara? Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Inter-madhhab dispute on zina and musahara prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi and Shafi'i positions on whether zina creates musahara prohibition and explain the Hanafi proof based on the cause of partial connection.

Core Idea
Zina creates marriage prohibition because intercourse causes partial kinship, despite being unlawful.

Does an unlawful act like zina carry the same legal consequences as lawful marriage? The Hanafi school argues yes regarding marriage prohibitions through affinity (musahara). The Shafi'i school disagrees, viewing the prohibition as a blessing unattainable through sin. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi reasoning grounded in the cause of lineage.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school holds that zina, touching, and looking with desire create the prohibition of musahara (marrying the ascendants/descendants of the person involved).
This is the mufta bihi position in the school.
2
State the Shafi'i objection
Identify that Imam al-Shafi'i argues that musahara prohibition is a blessing (ni'mah) and cannot be attained through a prohibited act.
3
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal
Understand that the Hanafi response focuses on the cause ('illa): intercourse causes a potential child, creating a partial connection (juz'iyyah) between the man and the woman's relatives, regardless of the lawfulness of the act.
The prohibition is a legal consequence, not a reward.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical difference: a Hanafi man cannot marry the mother or daughter of a woman he committed zina with; a Shafi'i can.
This affects real-world marriage options.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والزنا واللمس والنظر بشهوة يوجب حرمة المصاهرة وقال الشافعي : الزنا لا يوجب حرمة المصاهرة لأنها نعمة فلا تنال بالمحظور. ولنا أن الوطء سبب الجزئية بواسطة الولد حتى يضاف إلى كل واحد منهما كملاً فيصير أصولها وفروعها كأصوله وفروعه وكذلك على العكس والاستمتاع بالجزء حرام إلا في موضع الضرورة وهي الموطوءة والوطء محرم من داع إلى الوطء فيقام حيث إنه سبب الولد لا من حيث إنه زنا واللمس والنظر سب مقامه
His saying: (And zina, touching, and looking with desire cause the prohibition of musahara.) And al-Shafi'i said: Zina does not cause the prohibition of musahara because it is a blessing, so it cannot be attained by a prohibited act. And we have [the proof] that intercourse is a cause of partial connection through the child, so that [the child] is attributed to each of them completely, thus her ascendants and descendants become like his ascendants and descendants, and vice versa. And enjoyment of a part is prohibited except in a place of necessity, which is the woman who is the object of intercourse. And intercourse is prohibited due to the motive to intercourse; so it stands in place [of lawful intercourse] because it is a cause of the child, not because it is zina. And touching and looking stand in its place.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This is an inter-madhhab dispute. Hanafi holds that zina, touching, and looking with desire create the marriage prohibition (musahara). Shafi'i argues that prohibition is a blessing (ni'mah) and cannot be attained through a haram act. Hanafi responds by arguing that the effective cause ('illa) is the act of intercourse itself, which leads to the possibility of a child, not the sinfulness. Thus, even in zina, the prohibition arises because the act can create a partial connection (juz'iyyah) between the man and the woman's ascendants/descendants, and vice versa. Touching and looking with desire are analogized to intercourse.

Key Terms
حرمة المصاهرة (hurmat al-musahara): The prohibition of marriage that arises by affinity (through marriage or through zina according to Hanafi).
الجزئية (al-juz'iyyah): The partial connection (shared lineage) between the man and the woman's relatives via a child.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the core Hanafi reasoning for why zina creates marriage prohibition?
A) Because zina is a major sin and thus carries severe consequences.
B) Because intercourse can produce a child, creating a partial connection between relatives.
C) Because a hadith explicitly states that zina causes prohibition.
D) Because of consensus among the companions.

Key Takeaway
For the Hanafi school, any act of intercourse (lawful or unlawful) that can produce a child establishes the prohibition of musahara.

Redundancy of 'Permanent' in Marriage Prohibition Rules
Critical note on the necessity of 'permanent' in prohibition formulation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school's definition of nikah (intercourse vs. contract) determines whether the qualification 'permanent' is needed in the rule prohibiting combining two women.

Core Idea
The need for 'permanent' in the prohibition depends on whether nikah means intercourse or contract.

In Hanafi marriage law, the prohibition of combining two women due to a relationship (e.g., a woman and her husband's daughter) is often qualified with the word 'permanent'. However, a super-commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq questions whether this qualification is always necessary. The answer hinges on the precise meaning of 'nikah' in the legal rule: if it refers to intercourse, the permanence is already implied; if it refers to the contract, the qualification is essential. This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its implications for legal formulation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Objection
The objector argues that the phrase 'ayyata faradta' (whichever you consider as a male) already covers cases where the prohibition is temporary, making the word 'permanent' unnecessary. Begin by locating the objector's claim in the passage.
The objector is unnamed; this is a common critical move in Hanafi commentaries.
2
Analyse the Two Meanings of Nikah
The passage states that if nikah means intercourse (or includes intercourse), then the condition 'ayyata faradta' suffices. If nikah means the contract alone, then 'permanent' is needed because a contract with both women would be forbidden even if the prohibition is not permanent. Distinguish these two scenarios.
Hanafi scholars differ on whether nikah in different contexts means intercourse, the contract, or both.
3
Apply the Distinction to the Author's Conclusion
The author criticises al-Durr al-Mukhtar for including both the qualification 'permanent' and the phrase 'ayyata faradta', arguing that one of them should suffice. He also reports Zafar's view that prohibition from one side alone is enough, without regard to permanence. Trace how this leads to the conclusion that the formulation should be streamlined.
This is a methodological refinement: avoiding redundancy in legal statements.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (والمراد بالحرمة الخ) اعترض بأنه لا حاجة إلى قيد التأبيد لإغناء قوله «أية فرضت ذكر إحرام النكاح فإن السيدة لو فرضت ذكر إجاز له وطء الأخرى. وهذا بناء على أن المراد بالنكاح الوطء أو ما يشمله ويشمل العقد ولذا لم يذكره في النهر، وأخرج هذه المسألة بقوله أية فرضت. نعم لو أريد بالنكاح العقد احتيج إليه إذ يحرم إيراد العقد حينئذ عليهما. وأما ما يأتي من استحسان إيراد العقد من السيد على الأمة فذاك للاحتياط وبه يعلم أن ذكر التأبيد وإخراج المسألة بقوله «أية فرضت كما في فعل في الدر المختار غير ظاهر، بل الواجب الاقتصار على أحدهما قوله : (نظر إلى مطلق الحرمة) قال في النهر : الظاهر أن هذا القول له التفات إلى أن الحرمة من أحد الجانبين كافية كما قال زفر : فحرم الجمع بين المرأة وبنت زوجها لا بالنظر إلى التأبيد وعدمه.
His saying: (And the meaning of hurma etc.) It was objected: There is no need for the qualification of perpetuity because his saying 'ayyata faradta dhikra ihram al-nikah' is sufficient. For if the male owner (abd?) were considered a male, he would be permitted to have intercourse with the other. This is based on the meaning of nikah as intercourse or what includes it and includes the contract. Hence he did not mention it in al-Nahr, and he extracted this issue with his saying 'ayyata faradta'. Yes, if by nikah is meant the contract, then it is needed, because then entering into a contract with both would be forbidden. As for what follows of istihsan of entering into a contract by the male owner upon the slave girl, that is for precaution. And from this it is known that mentioning perpetuity and extracting the issue with his saying 'ayyata faradta' as done in al-Durr al-Mukhtar is not apparent; rather, it is necessary to limit to one of them. His saying: (considering the absolute prohibition). He said in al-Nahr: The apparent is that this statement has regard to the fact that prohibition from one side is sufficient, as Zafar said: So the combination between a woman and her husband's daughter is prohibited not by consideration of perpetuity or its absence.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This is a super-commentary (hāshiya) on the earlier point about permanent prohibition. An objector argues that the condition 'ayyata faradta' (whichever you consider as a male) already covers the cases, so specifying 'permanent' is redundant if nikah means intercourse. However, if nikah means the contract, the qualification is needed. The author notes that al-Durr al-Mukhtar's approach of including both is not clear; one should suffice. Zafar's view is cited: prohibition from one side is enough, without regard to permanence.

Key Terms
التأبيد (al-ta'bid): Permanence as a quality of the prohibition; considered redundant if nikah means intercourse.
النكاح (المعنى) (al-nikah (al-ma'na)): Whether nikah in the rule means intercourse or the marriage contract.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the objector in the passage, when is the qualification 'permanent' not needed?
A) When nikah means the contract.
B) When nikah means intercourse.
C) When combining two slave women.
D) Never.

Key Takeaway
The need for 'permanent' in marriage prohibition rules hinges on the definition of nikah; Hanafi scholars refine formulations to avoid redundancy.

Prohibition of Marrying Two Women Related as Aunts
Explains the ruling on combining two women who are aunts to each other and the condition for prohibition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying two women who are mutual aunts, identify the condition (ayyatu furidat) that determines the prohibition, and explain the 'illa dispute.

Core Idea
Marrying two women who are mutual aunts is haram if, hypothetically, one were male and the other would be a mahram.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq explores the prohibition of combining two women who are each the aunt of the other. It establishes that the ruling is derived by analogy from the prohibition of combining two sisters, with the effective cause being fear of severing family ties. The text also introduces a critical conditional tool—'if it were supposed'—which distinguishes between permanent and temporary prohibitions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the ruling
Recognize the specific relationships (e.g., two women who are aunts to each other via marriage or fosterage) and note that the Hanafi school rules this combination as haram.
The prohibition is based on the analogy to combining two sisters.
2
Understand the condition 'ayyatu furidat'
This condition tests whether the marriage would be prohibited if one of the women were male. If the hypothetical male would be a mahram to the other, the combination is haram.
It is a tool to distinguish permanent prohibitions from temporary ones.
3
Analyse the 'illa dispute
Some Hanafi scholars (from al-Mabsut) argued the 'illa (cause) is not fear of severance for foster sisters, but the author refutes this using the hadith 'What is forbidden by fosterage is forbidden by lineage.'
The accepted view is that the cause is fear of severing family ties.
4
Apply to provided examples
Work through the examples: woman and husband's daughter, woman and son's wife, and the case of Abdullah ibn Ja'far. Verify that the condition determines permissibility.
Temporary prohibitions (e.g., due to ownership) do not invoke this condition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذكور فيتخرج عليه حرمة الجمع بين عمتين وخالتين وذلك أن يتزوج كل من الرجلين أم الآخر فيولد لكل منهما بنت فتكون كل من البنتين عمة للأخرى، أو يتزوج كل من رجلين بنت الآخر ويولد لهما بنتان فكل من البنتين خالة للأخرى. وبما قرر علم أن العلة خوف القطيعة، وظهر به ضعف ما قدمناه عن المبسوط من أن العلة ليس ذلك إذ لا قرابة بين الأختين رضاعاً. وجوابه أن حرمة الجمع بينهما للحديث يحرم من الرضاع ما يحرم من النسب. والمراد بالحرمة في قوله حرم النكاح الحرمة المؤبدة، أما المؤقتة فلا تمنع ولذا لو تزوج أمة ثم سيدتها فإنه يجوز كما في الجامع والزيادات لأنها حرمة مؤقتة بزوال ملك اليمين. وقيل: لا يجوز تزوج السيدة عليها نظراً إلى مطلق الحرمة كما في القنية. وقيد بقوله «أية فرضت» لأنه لو جاز نكاح إحداهما على تقدير مثل المرأة وبنت زوجها أو امرأة ابنها فإنه يجوز الجمع بينهما عند الأئمة الأربعة، وقد جمع عبد الله بن جعفر بين زوجة علي وبنته ولم ينكر عليه أحد . وبيانه أنه لو فرضت بنت الزوج ذكراً بأن كان ابن الزوج لم يجز له أن يتزوج بها لأنها موطوءة أبيه ، ولو فرضت المرأة ذكراً لجاز له أن يتزوج ببنت الزوج لأنها بنت رجل أجنبي، وكذلك بين المرأة وامرأة ابنها فإن المرأة لو فرضت ذكراً لحرم عليه التزوج بامرأة ابنه، ولو فرضت امرأة الابن ذكراً لجاز له التزوج بالمرأة لأنه أجنبي عنها. قالوا: ولا بأس أن يتزوج الرجل امرأة ويتزوج ابنه أمها أو بنتها لأنه لا مانع وقد تزوج محمد بن الحنفية امرأة وزوج ابنه بنتها .

قوله : (والمراد بالحرمة الخ) اعترض بأنه لا حاجة إلى قيد التأبيد لإغناء قوله «أية فرضت ذكر إحرام النكاح فإن السيدة لو فرضت ذكر إجاز له وطء الأخرى. وهذا بناء على أن المراد بالنكاح الوطء أو ما يشمله ويشمل العقد ولذا لم يذكره في النهر، وأخرج هذه المسألة بقوله أية فرضت. نعم لو أريد بالنكاح العقد احتيج إليه إذ يحرم إيراد العقد حينئذ عليهما. وأما ما يأتي من استحسان إيراد العقد من السيد على الأمة فذاك للاحتياط وبه يعلم أن ذكر التأبيد وإخراج المسألة بقوله «أية فرضت كما في فعل في الدر المختار غير ظاهر، بل الواجب الاقتصار على أحدهما

قوله : (نظر إلى مطلق الحرمة) قال في النهر : الظاهر أن هذا القول له التفات إلى أن الحرمة من أحد الجانبين كافية كما قال زفر : فحرم الجمع بين المرأة وبنت زوجها لا بالنظر إلى التأبيد وعدمه.
From what was mentioned, the prohibition of combining two maternal aunts and two paternal aunts follows. That is, if each of two men marries the mother of the other, and each has a daughter, then each of the two daughters is a paternal aunt of the other; or if each of two men marries the daughter of the other, and each has a daughter, then each of the two daughters is a maternal aunt of the other. From this it is known that the cause is fear of severance, and the weakness of what we previously mentioned from al-Mabsut—that the cause is not that, since there is no lineage between two foster-sisters—becomes apparent. The answer is that the prohibition of combining them is due to the hadith: 'What is forbidden by fosterage is forbidden by lineage.' And what is meant by 'prohibition' in his statement 'marriage is prohibited' is the permanent prohibition. As for temporary prohibition, it does not prevent, so if a man marries a slave-woman and then her mistress, it is permissible, as in al-Jami' and al-Ziyadat, because it is a temporary prohibition due to removal of ownership. Some say: it is not permissible to marry the mistress over her, considering the absolute prohibition, as in al-Qunyah. And it is qualified by his statement 'if it were supposed' because if the marriage of one of them were permissible on the hypothetical supposition—like a woman and the daughter of her husband, or the wife of her son—then it is permissible to combine them according to the four imams. Abdullah ibn Ja'far combined the wife of Ali and his daughter, and no one objected. Its explanation: if the husband's daughter were supposed male, i.e., the husband's son, he could not marry her because she is his father's wife; and if the woman were supposed male, it would be permissible for him to marry the husband's daughter because she is the daughter of a unrelated man. Similarly for a woman and her son's wife: if the woman were supposed male, it would be prohibited for him to marry his son's wife; and if the son's wife were supposed male, it would be permissible for him to marry the woman because she is unrelated to him. They said: there is no harm in a man marrying a woman and his son marrying her mother or her daughter, because there is no impediment. Muhammad ibn al-Hanafiyyah married a woman and married his son to her daughter.

His statement: (And what is meant by prohibition...) It is objected that there is no need for the qualification of permanence because his statement 'if it were supposed' suffices to indicate the prohibition of marriage; for if the mistress were supposed male, he would be allowed intercourse with the other. This is based on the understanding that 'marriage' means intercourse or what includes it and includes the contract. Hence, he did not mention it in al-Nahr, and he addressed this issue with his statement 'if it were supposed.' Yes, if marriage means the contract, then it is needed, because then entering into the contract is prohibited with both. As for what follows about the permissibility of the master entering into the contract with the slave-woman, that is for caution. Thus it is known that mentioning permanence and removing the issue with 'if it were supposed' as done in al-Durr al-Mukhtar is not apparent; rather, one should suffice with one of them.

His statement: (Consideration of the absolute prohibition) It is said in al-Nahr: The apparent meaning is that this statement considers that prohibition from one side is sufficient, as Zufar said: Thus the combination of a woman and her husband's daughter is prohibited, without regard to permanence or not.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the prohibition of marrying two women who are in a mutual aunt relationship (i.e., each is the aunt of the other). The author explains that this prohibition is derived by analogy from the case of combining two sisters, where the cause is fear of severing family ties. He rejects an earlier opinion from al-Mabsut that denied this cause for foster-sisters, citing the hadith 'What is forbidden by fosterage is forbidden by lineage.' The passage then clarifies that the prohibition under discussion is permanent, not temporary; temporary prohibitions (like those due to ownership) do not prevent combining. The author also introduces the important condition 'if it were supposed' (أية فرضت): the marriage of two women is only prohibited if, were one of them male, the other would be a mahram (unmarriageable). This is illustrated with examples including a woman and her husband's daughter, and a woman and her son's wife, and the historical example of Abdullah ibn Ja'far. The subsequent commentary addresses objections about the need to mention permanence and clarifies the Hanafi position.

Key Terms
حرمة المصاهرة (ḥurmat al-muṣāhara): The prohibition of marriage due to affinity (in-laws).
علة (ʿilla): The effective cause or rationale behind a legal ruling.
أية فرضت (ayyatu furiḍat): A condition applied in determining prohibition: 'if it were presumed that one of them is male'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the condition expressed by 'أية فرضت' in the context of prohibiting marriage between two women?
A) That the women must be blood relatives.
B) That if one of the women were male, marriage with the other would be prohibited.
C) That the marriage must already be contracted.
D) That the women must be of different religions.

Key Takeaway
The prohibition of marrying two women who are mutual aunts depends on the hypothetical condition 'if one were male'; the Hanafi school bases it on the hadith of fosterage.

Zina Establishes Affinity: Hanafi Proof and Shafi'i Refutation
Proves zina causes affinity and refutes Shafi'i objection

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that zina causes the prohibition of affinity and refute the Shafi'i objection using the child's honor as the basis.

Core Idea
Affinity is established by intercourse, not its legality; the child's honor is the cause.

This lesson addresses a key inter-madhhab dispute: does zina (fornication) create the same prohibition of marriage due to affinity (muṣāhara) as lawful marriage? The Hanafi school says yes, while Imam al-Shafi'i disagrees, arguing that a blessing cannot be attained through a prohibited act. We will trace the Hanafi proof, which focuses on the act of intercourse leading to the creation of a child, and see how they respond to the Shafi'i objection using a subtle analogy.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the exact ruling: zina with a woman makes her mother and daughter mahram to the man, and his father and son mahram to her, just as in lawful marriage.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection
Recognize the opposing argument: affinity is a blessing (ni'mah), so it cannot arise from a sinful act like zina.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof based on the child's honor
The Hanafi response: the ruling is not based on the act's legality but on the fact that intercourse is the cause of the child, who is honored (Quran 17:70). The child has no sin, so the prohibition follows from the child's existence, not the act's sinfulness.
The text uses the analogy of tayammum: earth substitutes for water despite being impure, because the goal is purification.
4
Understand the conditions
Note the prerequisites: the woman must be alive; intercourse must be vaginal (front). Sodomy (liwat) does not cause affinity according to the majority, as it does not lead to a child.
Some later Hanafi scholars differed on sodomy, but the mufta bihi view is that it does not cause affinity.
5
Evaluate the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
Under Hanafi law, a man who commits zina with a woman cannot later marry her mother or daughter; under Shafi'i law, he can.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (من حيث أنه في موضع الاحتياط كذا في الهداية ولم يستدل بقوله تعالى ولا تنكحوا ما نكح آباؤكم [النساء : ٢٢] كما فعل الشارحون لما قدمنا أنه لا يصلح الاستدلال به. أراد بالزنا الوطء الحرام وإنما قيد به لأنه محل الخلاف، أما لو وطئ المنكوحة نكاحاً فاسداً أو المشتراة فاسداً أو الجارية المشتركة أو المكاتبة أو المظاهر منها أو الأمة المجوسية أو زوجته الحائض أو النفساء أو كان محرماً أو صائماً فإنه يثبت حرمة المصاهرة اتفاقاً وبه علم أن الاعتبار لعين الوطء لا لكونه حلالاً أو حراماً، وليفيد أنه لا بد أن تكون المرأة حية لأنه لو وطئ الميتة فإنه لا تثبت حرمة المصاهرة كما في الخانية وليفيد أنه لا بد أن يكون في القبل لأنه لو وطئ المرأة في الدبر) قال الكاكي رحمه الله تعالى : أما لو لاط بغلام لا يوجب ذلك حرمة عند عامة العلماء إلا عند أحمد والأوزاعي فإن تحريم المصاهرة عندهما يتعلق باللواطة حتى تحرم عليه أم الغلام وبنته ا هـ . وفي الغاية والجماع في الدبر لا يوجب حرمة المصاهرة وبه بعض مشايخنا، وقيل يوجبها وبه كان يفتي شمس الأئمة الأوزجندي لأنه مس وزيادة. قال صاحب الذخيرة : وما ذكره محمد أولاً أصح لعدم إفضائه إلى الجزئية .

فإنه سبب الولد قال ابن أمير حاج في شرح التحرير فإن قيل ثبوت حرمة المصاهرة نعمة لأنها تلحق الأجنبيات بالأمهات والأجانب بالآباء وقد ثبتت مسببة عن الزنا عند الحنفية وهو تناقض ظاهر لأنه يفيد جعل الزنا مشروعاً بعد النهي فالجواب منع ثبوتها مسببة عن الزنا من حيث ذاته بل من حيث للماء الذي هو سبب البعضية الحاصلة بالولد الذي هو مستحق الكرامات ومنها حرمة المحارم إقامة للسبب الظاهر المفضي إلى المسبب الحقي مقامه كما في الوطء الحلال لأن الوقوف على حقيقة العلوق متعذر، والولد عين لا معصية فيه ثم يتعدى حرمة أبي الواطئ وأبنائه من الولد إلى الموطوءة، وحرمة أمهات الموطوءة وبناتها منه أيضاً إلى الواطئ لصيرورة كل من الواطئ والموطوءة بعضاً . عن الآخر بواسطة الولد لأن الولد مخلوق من مائهما ومضاف إلى كل منهما، وهذا هو المراد بقوله وثبوت حرمة المصاهرة عنده أي الزنا بأمر آخر لا بالزنا» ا هـ . عبارة ابن أمير حاج في شرح التحرير، وقال الحلبي محشي الزيلعي : وهذا جواب لقول الشافعي إن حرمة المصاهرة نعمة فلا تنال بالمحظور، بيانه أن الوطء يثبت حرمة المصاهرة لا من حيث إنه زنا، بل من حيث أنه سبب الولد المخلوق من المائين، والولد محترم مكرم داخل تحت قوله (ولقد كرمنا بني آدم [الإسراء: ٧٠] فليس فيه صفة القبح لأنه مخلوق بخلق الله تعالى على أي وجه اجتمع الماءان في الرحم ألا ترى إلى قوله تعالى ثم أنشأناه خلقاً آخر ﴾ [المؤمنون: ١٤] فلما لم يكن في الأصل وهو الولد صفة القبح صار المنظور إليه هو الذي قام مقامه وهو الوطء كالتراب لما قام مقام الماء عند عدمه صار المنظور صفة الماء في إثبات الطهارة لا صفة التراب الذي هو تلويث فلم يرد علينا قول الشافعي أن الزنا محظور لا يثبت به ما سبيله النعمة والكرامة لأن الزنا ليس بمنظور إليه في إيجاب حرمة المصاهرة فافهم . ا هـ عبارة الحلبي .
His statement: (Because it is a matter of caution, thus in al-Hidayah, and he did not use as evidence the verse 'And do not marry what your fathers married' [4:22] as the commentators did, because we mentioned that it is not suitable as evidence. By zina he means unlawful intercourse, and it is qualified because it is the point of disagreement. As for if he had intercourse with a woman married with a invalid contract, or one bought with an invalid purchase, or a shared slave-girl, or a mukatabah, or one from whom he had made zihar, or a magian slave-girl, or his wife during menstruation or postpartum, or if he were in ihram or fasting, then the prohibition of affinity is established by agreement. From this it is known that consideration is given to the act of intercourse itself, not to whether it is halal or haram. And it benefits that the woman must be alive; if he had intercourse with a dead woman, the prohibition of affinity is not established, as in al-Khaniyyah. And it benefits that the intercourse must be in the front; if he had intercourse with a woman in the anus... al-Kaki said: As for sodomy with a boy, it does not cause prohibition according to the general scholars, except according to Ahmad and al-Awza'i, for the prohibition of affinity according to them is connected with sodomy, so that the mother and daughter of the boy become prohibited to him. In al-Ghayah: Intercourse in the anus does not cause prohibition of affinity; some of our scholars hold this. Some say it does cause it, and Shams al-A'imma al-Awzjandi used to give fatwa according to this, because it is touch and more. The author of al-Dhakhira said: What Muhammad mentioned first is more correct because it does not lead to partiality.

Because it is the cause of the child. Ibn Amir Hajj said in Sharh al-Tahrir: If it is said that the establishing of prohibition of affinity is a blessing because it joins unrelated women to mothers and unrelated men to fathers, and it is established as a result of zina according to the Hanafis, which is an apparent contradiction because it would make zina legitimate after prohibition. The answer is to deny that it is established as a result of zina in its essence, but rather due to the fluid which is the cause of the partiality resulting from the child, who is deserving of honors, including the prohibition of mahrams. It is a substitution of the apparent cause that leads to the real cause, as in lawful intercourse, because ascertaining the reality of conception is impossible. The child is an entity with no sin in it. Then the prohibition extends from the father and sons of the fornicator from the child to the fornicated woman, and from the mothers and daughters of the fornicated woman from him to the fornicator, because each becomes part of the other through the child, since the child is created from their fluids and attributed to each. This is what is meant by his statement: 'And the establishment of prohibition of affinity according to him, i.e., zina, is due to something else, not due to zina.' End quote from Ibn Amir Hajj in Sharh al-Tahrir. Al-Halabi, the commentator of al-Zayla'i, said: This is a response to al-Shafi'i's statement that the prohibition of affinity is a blessing and cannot be attained by a prohibited act. Its explanation: intercourse establishes the prohibition of affinity not because it is zina, but because it is the cause of the child created from the two fluids. The child is honored and dignified, included in His saying 'And We have certainly honored the children of Adam' [17:70]. There is no attribute of ugliness in it because it is created by Allah's creation regardless of how the two fluids come together in the womb. Do you not see His saying 'Then We made it another creation' [23:14]? So when the original, which is the child, has no attribute of ugliness, what is looked at is that which stands in its place, i.e., intercourse, like earth when it stands in place of water in its absence: what is looked at is the attribute of water in establishing purity, not the attribute of earth which is soiling. So the statement of al-Shafi'i that zina is prohibited and does not establish something whose path is blessing and honor does not apply to us, because zina is not looked at in causing the prohibition of affinity. Understand this. End quote from al-Halabi.
Source pages p. 173

Commentary
This passage addresses the inter-madhhab dispute regarding whether zina (fornication) establishes the prohibition of affinity (muṣāhara). The Hanafi position is that it does, while Imam al-Shafi'i holds that it does not because affinity is a blessing and cannot be attained through a prohibited act. The author first clarifies that by 'zina' here is meant unlawful intercourse, and that the disagreement is specifically about that; other types of intercourse (invalid marriage, etc.) are agreed upon. The Hanafi proof is based on the principle that what matters is the act of intercourse itself, not its legality, because the act leads to the creation of a child, which is honored. The text provides a detailed response to Shafi'i through the commentary of Ibn Amir Hajj and al-Halabi, using the analogy of tayammum: just as earth substitutes for water in purification despite being impure, so too does unlawful intercourse substitute for lawful in establishing affinity because the child is the real cause, and the child is honorable. The passage also discusses conditions: the woman must be alive, and the intercourse must be in the front (vaginal). The text then addresses the specific issue of sodomy (liwat), noting that the majority of scholars do not consider it to cause affinity, although some (Ahmad, al-Awza'i) disagree.

Key Terms
حرمة المصاهرة (ḥurmat al-muṣāhara): Prohibition of marriage due to affinity, including relationships established through marriage or valid intercourse, and according to Hanafi, also through zina.
الزنا (al-zinā): Unlawful sexual intercourse between a man and a woman who are not married.
الوطء (al-waṭʾ): Sexual intercourse. The text distinguishes between halal and haram intercourse for the purpose of establishing affinity.
الولد (al-walad): Child. The child is the real cause of the prohibition of affinity, regardless of whether the intercourse was lawful or unlawful.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the primary basis for the Hanafi ruling that zina causes the prohibition of affinity?
A) Zina is analogous to marriage in all respects.
B) The child produced from the act is honored, and the prohibition follows from the child's existence.
C) The Prophet ﷺ explicitly stated it in a hadith.
D) Zina is not a sin in this context.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, zina establishes the same prohibition of affinity as lawful marriage because the act can produce a child, and the child is honored regardless of how it was conceived.
