Permissibility of Marrying Kitabi Women: Proof and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Commentary on the permissibility of marrying Kitabi women with proofs and internal disagreement

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying Kitabi women, cite the Quranic proof, and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement regarding those who believe in the Trinity.

Core Idea
Marriage to Kitabi women is permissible; the relied-upon view allows even Trinitarians.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq explains the ruling on marrying women from the People of the Book. It presents the Quranic verse, addresses an objection from Ibn Umar, and then navigates an internal Hanafi debate about whether belief in the Trinity affects permissibility. You will learn how the Hanafi school applies the verse and which position is relied upon for fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and primary proof
The matn states 'wa halla tazawwuj al-kitabiyyah' — it is permissible. The proof is Quran 5:5: 'wa al-muhsanat min alladhina utu al-kitab'. Note that the word 'muhsanat' (chaste) indicates recommendation (nadb), not a condition.
The verse is qat'i al-thubut and qat'i al-dalalah according to Hanafi.
2
Address the counterargument from Ibn Umar
Ibn Umar considered Kitabi women polytheists because they worship Messiah/Ezra. The majority refute this by citing Quran 98:1, which distinguishes 'Ahl al-Kitab' from 'mushrikun' via conjunction, implying legal separation.
3
Define Ahl al-Kitab according to Hanafi school
The Hanafi school broadly includes anyone with a revealed scripture (e.g., Sabians, followers of Ibrahim, Sheet). This is wider than Shafi'i, who restricts to Jews and Christians.
This affects not only marriage but also eating their slaughter.
4
Navigate the intra-Hanafi debate on Trinity belief
Some Hanafis (e.g., al-Mustasfa, Mabsut Shaykh al-Islam) restrict permissibility if the woman believes Jesus or Ezra is God. Others (Shams al-A'imma, Fath al-Qadir) permit absolutely. The relied-upon view is absolute permissibility because the Quranic text is unconditional and those holding such beliefs are from extinct groups.
The mufta bihi is absolute permissibility.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وحل تزوج الكتابية) لقوله تعالى ﴿ والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب ﴾ [المائدة: ٥] أي العفائف عن الزنا بياناً للندب لا أن العفة فيهن شرط. وعن ابن عمر أنها لا تحل لأنها مشركة لأنهم يعبدون المسيح وعزيراً، وحمل المحصنات في الآية على من أسلم منهن. وللجمهور أن المشرك ليس من أهل الكتاب للعطف في قوله تعالى ﴿ لم يكن الذين كفروا من أهل الكتاب والمشركين ﴾ [البينة : ١] والعطف يقتضي المغايرة. وفي قوله تعالى ﴿ لتجدن أشد الناس عداوة للذين آمنوا اليهود والذين أشركوا ﴾ [المائدة: ۸۲] وفي التبيين : ثم كل من يعتقد ديناً سماوياً وله كتاب منزل كصحف إبراهيم وشيث وزبور داود فهو من أهل الكتاب فتجوز مناكحتهم وأكل ذبائحهم خلافاً للشافعي فيما عدا اليهود والنصارى والحجة عليه ما تلونا. وفي فتح القدير: الكتابي من يؤمن بنبي ويقر بكتاب والسامرية من اليهود. أطلق المصنف الكتابية هنا وقيدها في المستصفى بقوله : قالوا هذا يعني الحل إذا لم يعتقد المسيح إلها، أما إذا اعتقده فلا ويوافقه ما في مبسوط شيخ الإسلام ويجب أن لا يأكلوا ذبائح أهل الكتاب إذا اعتقدوا أن المسيح إله وأن عزيراً إله، ولا يتزوجوا نساءهم. قيل : وعليه الفتوى ولكن بالنظر إلى الدلائل ينبغي أنه يجوز الأكل والتزوج ا هـ. وحاصله أن المذهب الإطلاق لما ذكره شمس الأئمة في المبسوط من أن ذبيحة النصراني حلال مطلقاً، سواء قال بثالث ثلاثة أولا لإطلاق الكتاب هنا والدليل. ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن القائل بذلك طائفتان من اليهود والنصارى انقرضوا لا كلهم مع أن مطلق لفظ المشرك إذا ذكر في لسان أهل الشرع لا ينصرف إلى أهل الكتاب وإن صح لغة في طائفة أو طوائف لما عهد من إرادته به من عبد مع الله غيره ممن لا يدعي اتباع نبي وكتاب إلى آخر ما ذكره. وفي معراج الدراية : اختلف العلماء في أن لفظ المشرك يتناول أهل الكتاب والأصح أن اسم المشرك مطلقاً لا يتناوله للعطف في الآية. ثم المشرك ثلاثة : مشرك ظاهراً وباطناً كعبدة الأوثان، ومشرك باطناً لا ظاهراً كالمنافقين ومشرك معنى كأهل الكتاب. ففي قوله سبحانه وتعالى
His statement: (And the permissibility of marrying a Kitabi woman) due to the saying of Allah, Exalted: 'And the chaste women from those who were given the Scripture before you' [al-Ma'idah 5:5] i.e., those chaste from adultery, as an indication of recommendation, not that chastity is a condition in them. And it is narrated from Ibn Umar that she is not permissible because she is a polytheist, since they worship the Messiah and Ezra, and he interpreted 'muhsanat' in the verse as those who became Muslims among them. And for the majority, the polytheist is not from the People of the Book due to the conjunction in the verse: 'Those who disbelieve from the People of the Book and the polytheists' [al-Bayyinah 98:1], and conjunction requires difference. And in His saying: 'You will surely find the most intense of the people in enmity to the believers the Jews and those who associate partners with Allah' [al-Ma'idah 5:82]. And in al-Tabyin: then everyone who believes in a heavenly religion and has a revealed book like the scriptures of Ibrahim, Sheet, and Zabur Dawud, he is from the People of the Book, so marrying them and eating their slaughtered meat is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding those other than Jews and Christians, and the proof against him is what we recited. And in Fath al-Qadir: the Kitabi is one who believes in a prophet and affirms a book, and the Samaritans are from the Jews. The author generalized the Kitabi woman here but restricted in al-Mustasfa by saying: they said this means permissibility if they do not believe the Messiah is God; if they believe that, then it is not. And what is in Mabsut of Shaykh al-Islam agrees with it: you must not eat the slaughtered meat of the People of the Book if they believe that the Messiah is God and that Ezra is God, and do not marry their women. It was said: and upon it is the fatwa, but with regard to the evidences, it is appropriate that eating and marrying are permissible. The summary is that the school is unrestricted, as Shams al-A'imma mentioned in al-Mabsut: the slaughtered meat of a Christian is absolutely permissible, whether he says with a third of three or not, due to the absolute wording of the book and the evidence. And Fath al-Qadir favored it, because those who say that (i.e., Trinity) are two groups of Jews and Christians who have become extinct, not all of them. Moreover, the absolute term 'polytheist' when mentioned in the language of the Law does not refer to the People of the Book, even if it is linguistically correct for some groups, because of the customary usage of the term for those who worship alongside Allah someone else who does not claim to follow a prophet and a book, and so on. And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: the scholars differed on whether the term 'polytheist' includes the People of the Book, and the correct view is that the name 'polytheist' absolutely does not include them, due to the conjunction in the verse. Then the polytheist is of three types: a polytheist outwardly and inwardly like idolaters, a polytheist inwardly not outwardly like hypocrites, and a polytheist in meaning like the People of the Book. In His saying, Exalted: ...
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling that it is permissible to marry a Kitabi woman (from the People of the Book). The author begins by citing the Quranic verse (5:5) as proof. He clarifies that the term 'muhsanat' (chaste women) indicates recommendation not condition. He then presents an opposing view from Ibn Umar who considered them polytheists. The majority refute this by noting that the Quran distinguishes between 'People of the Book' and 'polytheists' (98:1). The author then expands the definition of 'Ahl al-Kitab' to include anyone with a divine scripture, contrary to Shafi'i who restricts to Jews and Christians. He then discusses an internal Hanafi distinction: some scholars like the author of al-Mustasfa and Shaykh al-Islam in al-Mabsut restrict permissibility to those who do not believe in the divinity of Jesus or Ezra. However, the preferred view (from Shams al-A'imma and Fath al-Qadir) is that it is absolutely permissible because those who hold such beliefs are extinct groups, and the term 'polytheist' in shariah does not include Ahl al-Kitab. The passage ends with a classification of polytheism.

Key Terms
الكتابية (al-kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book (those who follow a revealed scripture).
المحصنات (al-muhsanat): Chaste women, specifically those free from adultery. In this context, it indicates recommendation, not a condition for permissibility.
المشرك (al-mushrik): One who associates partners with Allah. The passage distinguishes different types.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marriage to any Kitabi woman, with the relied-upon view allowing even those who believe in the Trinity, based on the absolute Quranic text and the legal distinction between Ahl al-Kitab and polytheists.

Marriage Between Hanafis and Shafi'is and With Non-Muslims
Ruling on marriage between sects and permissibility of marrying polytheists

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on marriage between Hanafis and Shafi'is and explain the prohibition of marrying polytheist women, distinguishing between the Hanafi position and the minority view.

Core Idea
Marriage between Hanafis and Shafi'is is valid; marrying polytheist women is haram, but non-Muslim men of different sects may intermarry.

This lesson addresses two important issues: the validity of marriage between Muslims of different legal schools (Hanafis and Shafi'is) and the prohibition of marrying polytheist women. The author clarifies that sectarian differences do not affect the validity of marriage among Muslims. Regarding polytheist women, the majority of scholars forbid marriage based on the Quranic verse, though a minority permitted intercourse with captives. The Hanafi ruling is clear in prohibiting such marriages, while allowing intermarriage among People of the Book.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties and scenarios
The passage covers three scenarios: (1) marriage between Hanafis and Shafi'is, (2) Muslim marriage to polytheist women, and (3) intermarriage among non-Muslims. First, identify each scenario and the ruling stated.
The ruling for Mu'tazilites is also mentioned but secondary.
2
Extract the legal proof for each ruling
For scenario (1), the proof is that both are Muslims and Shafi'is do not declare Hanafis disbelievers. For (2), the primary proof is the Quranic verse prohibiting polytheist women. For (3), the proof is the statement from al-Khaniyya that non-Muslims (except apostates) can intermarry.
The minority view for (2) relies on a historical incident, but the majority view prevails.
3
Analyze the ikhtilaf on polytheist women
Note the dispute between the majority (including Hanafis) and Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and a group. The majority forbids based on the Quran; the minority allows based on the captives of Awtas. The Hanafi response is that those captives may have converted, and the general prohibition stands.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the tradition.
4
Apply the ruling to modern contexts
For a Hanafi-Shafi'i marriage today: valid. For a Muslim man wanting to marry a polytheist (e.g., Hindu idol worshipper): haram. For a Jewish man marrying a Christian woman: permissible.
Ensure correct classification of non-Muslim groups (e.g., Zoroastrians as non-scriptuary).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ويجب حمل كلامهم على من يقول ذلك شاكاً في إيمانه والشافعية لا يقولون به فتجوز المناكحة بين الحنفية والشافعية بلا شبهة وأما المعتزلة فمقتضى الوجه حل مناكحتهم لأن الحق عدم تكفير أهل القبلة كما قدمنا نقله عن الأئمة في باب الإمامة. وأفاد بحرمة نكاحهما حرمة وطئهما أيضاً بملك اليمين خلافاً لسعيد بن المسيب وجماعة لورود الإطلاق في سبايا العرب كأوطاس وغيرها وهن مشركات، وعامة العلماء منعوا من ذلك لللآية، فإما إن يراد بالنكاح الوطء أو كل منه ومن العقد بناء على أنه مشترك في سياق النفي أو خاص في الضم وهو ظاهر في الأمرين ويمكن كون سبايا أوطاس أسلمن. وقيدنا بالمسلم لما في الخانية: وتحل المجوسية والوثنية لكل كافر إلا المرتد ا هـ . يعني يجوز تزوج اليهودي نصرانية أو مجوسية وعكسه جائز لأنهم أهل ملة واحدة من حيث الكفر وإن اختلفت نحلهم.
And it is necessary to interpret their statement as referring to one who says that while doubting his faith, and the Shafi'is do not say it, so marriage between Hanafis and Shafi'is is permissible without any doubt. As for the Mu'tazilites, the apparent view is that marrying them is permissible because the correct view is not to declare the people of the qibla as disbelievers, as we have previously transmitted from the imams in the chapter on imamate. And it [the text] indicates that the prohibition of marrying them also implies the prohibition of sexual intercourse through right hand possession, contrary to Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and a group, due to the general application in the captives of the Arabs like Awtas and others, and they were polytheist women. The majority of scholars forbade that due to the verse. So either by 'marriage' is meant intercourse or each of the two, or the contract based on it being shared in the context of negation or specific in the pronoun, and it is apparent in both matters, and it is possible that the captives of Awtas had converted to Islam. And we restricted it to the Muslim because in al-Khaniyya: 'The Zoroastrian and idolatress are permissible for every disbeliever except the apostate.' That is, it is permissible for a Jewish man to marry a Christian or Zoroastrian woman and vice versa because they are all one religious community in terms of disbelief even if their sects differ.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on marriage between members of different Islamic sects and between Muslims and non-Muslims. The author first addresses the ruling on marriage between Hanafis and Shafi'is. He states that their statements should be interpreted as coming from someone who doubts the faith of the other, but the Shafi'is do not hold that view, so marriage between the two schools is permissible without any doubt. Regarding the Mu'tazilites, the apparent view is that marrying them is permissible because the correct position is not to declare any person who prays towards the qibla as a disbeliever, as transmitted from the imams. Next, the author discusses the prohibition of marrying polytheist women, which also includes sexual intercourse through right hand possession (i.e., taking them as captives). This is contrary to Sa'id ibn al-Musayyib and a group who permitted it based on the general application in the captives of Awtas who were polytheists. However, the majority of scholars forbid it based on the Quranic verse. The author notes that the word 'nikah' can mean intercourse or the contract, but in the context of negation it is ambiguous. It is possible that the captives of Awtas had converted to Islam. Finally, the author restricts the ruling to Muslims, citing al-Khaniyya that a Zoroastrian or idolatress is permissible for a disbeliever (except an apostate), meaning a Jewish man can marry a Christian or Zoroastrian woman and vice versa because they all share the same status of disbelief despite different sects.

Key Terms
مشرك (mushrik): One who associates partners with Allah; in this context, includes polytheists and those who worship idols.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Marriage between Muslims of different schools is valid; Muslims cannot marry polytheists, but non-Muslims of different sects may intermarry.

The Quranic Proof and Definition of Kitabiyyah
Ruling with proofs and inter-madhhab dispute on definition of kitabi.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on marrying a kitabiyyah based on Quran 5:5 and explain the Hanafi definition of 'kitabi'.

Core Idea
Marrying a Woman of the Book is permissible by Quran, but the definition of 'kitabi' is broad in Hanafi fiqh.

The permissibility of marrying a kitabiyyah is established by Quran 5:5. However, the scope of who qualifies as a 'kitabi' and the implications for marriage are debated among scholars. This lesson examines the primary proof and the difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools on this issue.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Quranic Verse
Locate the key verse (Quran 5:5) cited in the passage and note the phrase used as proof.
The verse is 'And the chaste women from those who were given the Book'.
2
Analyze the Term 'Muhsanat'
Understand the meaning of 'chaste' in the verse – is it a condition or a recommendation? The passage clarifies it is a recommendation, not a condition.
Hanafis hold that chastity is recommended (nadb), not a condition for validity.
3
Define Kitabi in Hanafi Fiqh
Extract the Hanafi definition: one who believes in a heavenly book and a prophet, including followers of Ibrahim, Seth, and Dawud.
This broad definition contrasts with the narrower view of other schools.
4
Compare with Shafi'i Definition
State the Shafi'i position that only Jews and Christians are considered Kitabi, and note the proof they might use.
The passage argues against this using Quranic conjunctions.
5
Determine the Practical Consequence
Explain the thamarah al-khilaf: Hanafis can marry Sabians and other scriptuaries, while Shafi'is cannot.
This difference has real-world implications for marital choices.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وحل تزوج الكتابية لقوله تعالى والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب [المائدة: ٥] أي العفائف عن الزنا بياناً للندب لا أن العفة فيهن شرط. وعن ابن عمر أنها لا تحل لأنها مشركة لأنهم يعبدون المسيح وعزيراً، وحمل المحصنات في الآية على من أسلم منهن. وللجمهور أن المشرك ليس من أهل الكتاب للعطف في قوله تعالى لم يكن الذين كفروا من أهل الكتاب والمشركين) [البينة : ١] والعطف يقتضي المغايرة. وفي قوله تعالى لتجدن أشد الناس عداوة للذين آمنوا اليهود والذين أشركوا ﴾ [المائدة: ۸۲] وفي التبيين : ثم كل من يعتقد ديناً سماوياً وله كتاب منزل كصحف إبراهيم وشيث وزبور داود فهو من أهل الكتاب فتجوز مناكحتهم وأكل ذبائحهم خلافاً للشافعي فيما عدا اليهود والنصارى والحجة عليه ما تلونا. وفي فتح القدير: الكتابي من يؤمن بنبي ويقر بكتاب والسامرية من اليهود. أطلق المصنف الكتابية هنا وقيدها في المستصفى بقوله : قالوا هذا يعني الحل إذا لم يعتقد المسيح إلها، أما إذا اعتقده فلا ويوافقه ما في مبسوط شيخ الإسلام ويجب أن لا يأكلوا ذبائح أهل الكتاب إذا اعتقدوا أن المسيح إله وأن عزيراً إله، ولا يتزوجوا نساءهم. قيل : وعليه الفتوى ولكن بالنظر إلى الدلائل ينبغي أنه يجوز الأكل والتزوج ا هـ. وحاصله أن المذهب الإطلاق لما ذكره شمس الأئمة في المبسوط من أن ذبيحة النصراني حلال مطلقاً، سواء قال بثالث ثلاثة أولا لإطلاق الكتاب هنا والدليل. ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن القائل بذلك طائفتان من اليهود والنصارى انقرضوا لا كلهم مع أن مطلق لفظ المشرك إذا ذكر في لسان أهل الشرع لا ينصرف إلى أهل الكتاب وإن صح لغة في طائفة أو طوائف لما عهد من إرادته به من عبد مع الله غيره ممن لا يدعي اتباع نبي وكتاب إلى آخر ما ذكره. وفي معراج الدراية : اختلف العلماء في أن لفظ المشرك يتناول أهل الكتاب والأصح أن اسم المشرك مطلقاً لا يتناوله للعطف في الآية. ثم المشرك ثلاثة : مشرك ظاهراً وباطناً كعبدة الأوثان، ومشرك باطناً لا ظاهراً كالمنافقين ومشرك معنى كأهل الكتاب. ففي قوله سبحانه وتعالى عما يشركون﴾ [يونس : ۱۸] المراد مطلق الشرك، وكذا في قوله تعالى إن الله لا يغفر أن يشرك به ﴾ [النساء : ١١٦] فيتناول جميع الكفار. وفي قوله ولا تنحكوا المشركات) [البقرة : ۲۲۱] المراد به المشرك ظاهراً وباطناً وهو الوثني فلا يتناول أهل الكتاب والمنافقين وأطلقه أيضاً فشمل الكتابية الحرة والأئمة، واتفق الأئمة الأربعة على حل الحرة واختلفوا في حل الأمة كما سيأتي هذا والأولى أن لا يتزوج كتابية ولا يأكل ذبائحهم إلا لضرورة. وفي المحيط : يكره تزوج الكتابية الحربية لأن الإنسان لا يأمن أن يكون بينهما ولد فينشأ على طبائع أهل الحرب ويتخلق بأخلاقهم فلا يستطيع المسلم قلعه عن تلك العادة ا هـ . أنها كراهة تنزية لأن التحريمية لا بد لها من نهي أو ما في معناه لأنها في رتبة الواجب. وفي الخانية : تزوج الحربية مكروه فإن خرج بها إلى دار الإسلام بقي النكاح ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه يحل وطء الكتابية بملك اليمين وسيأتي أن الكتابية إذا تمجست فإنه ينفسخ نكاحها من المسلم بخلاف اليهودية إذا تنصرت أو عكسه. وذكر الأسبيجابي أن للمسلم منع الذمية إذا تزوجها من الخروج إلى الكنائس والبيع وليس له إجبارها على الغسل من الحيض والجناية. وفي الخانية من فصل الجزية من السير: مسلم له امرأة ذمية ليس له أن يمنعها من شرب الخمر لأن شرب الخمر حلال عندها وله أن يمنعها عن اتخاذ الخمر في المنزل ا هـ. وهو مشكل لأنه وإن كان حلالاً عندها لكن رائحتها تضره فله منعها كمنع المسلمة من أكل الثوم والبصل ولذا قال الكركي في الفيض قبيل باب التيمم : إن المسلم له أن يمنع زوجته الذمية من شرب الخمر كالمسلمة لو أكلت الثوم والبصل وكان زوجها يكره ذلك له أن يمنعها ا هـ . وهذا هو الحق كما لا يخفى.
His statement: 'And the permissibility of marrying a kitabiyyah (woman of the Book) due to His saying: And the chaste women from those who were given the Book (Quran 5:5) — meaning the chaste ones from fornication, as an indication of recommendation, not that chastity is a condition in them. And from Ibn Umar that she is not permissible because she is a polytheist since they worship the Messiah and Ezra, and he interpreted 'the chaste women' in the verse as those who embraced Islam from them. And for the majority, the polytheist is not from the People of the Book due to the conjunction in His saying: Those who disbelieve from the People of the Book and the polytheists (Quran 98:1) and conjunction requires difference. And in His saying: You will surely find the most hostile of people to the believers are the Jews and those who associate partners (Quran 5:82). And in al-Tabyin: Then everyone who believes in a heavenly religion and has a revealed book like the scriptures of Ibrahim and Seth and the Psalms of Dawud is from the People of the Book, so marrying them is permissible and eating their slaughtered meat is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding other than Jews and Christians, and the proof against him is what we have recited. And in Fath al-Qadir: The kitabi is one who believes in a prophet and acknowledges a book, and the Samaritans are from the Jews. The author made the kitabiyyah unrestricted here and restricted it in al-Mustasfa by saying: They said this—meaning the permissibility—if she does not believe that the Messiah is God; if she believes that, then it is not permissible. And this is supported by what is in Mabsoot of Shaykh al-Islam: It is obligatory not to eat the slaughtered meat of the People of the Book if they believe that the Messiah is God and that Ezra is God, and not to marry their women. It is said that the fatwa is upon this, but considering the evidences, it seems that eating and marrying are permissible. The summary is that the madhhab is unrestricted as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma in al-Mabsoot that the slaughtered meat of a Christian is absolutely halal, whether he says Trinity or not, due to the unrestricted nature of the Book and the proof. And he preferred it in Fath al-Qadir because those who say that are two groups from the Jews and Christians who have become extinct, not all of them. Moreover, the unrestricted word 'polytheist' when mentioned in the language of the people of Shari'a does not apply to the People of the Book, even if it is linguistically correct for a group or groups, due to the established usage referring to one who worships other than Allah without claiming to follow a prophet and a book... And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: The scholars differed on whether the word 'polytheist' includes the People of the Book, and the correct view is that the name 'polytheist' absolutely does not include them due to the conjunction in the verse. Then the polytheist is three types: a polytheist outwardly and inwardly like idol worshippers, a polytheist inwardly not outwardly like hypocrites, and a polytheist in meaning like the People of the Book. In His saying: From what they associate (Quran 10:18), the intended meaning is absolute shirk, and similarly in His saying: Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him (Quran 4:116) includes all disbelievers. And in His saying: And do not marry polytheist women (Quran 2:221), the intended meaning is the polytheist outwardly and inwardly, which is the idol worshipper, so it does not include the People of the Book and the hypocrites. And he also made it unrestricted, so it includes the free kitabiyyah and the slaves. And the four imams agreed on the permissibility of the free one and differed on the permissibility of the slave as will come. And it is better not to marry a kitabiyyah nor to eat their slaughtered meat except for necessity. And in al-Muhit: It is disliked to marry a kitabiyyah from a warring territory because one cannot be sure that a child born between them will grow up with the habits of the people of war and adopt their character, so the Muslim cannot uproot him from that habit. This is a disliked (makruh tanzihi) because the prohibition requires a prohibition or what is in its meaning, as it is in the rank of obligation. And in al-Khaniyya: Marrying a woman from a warring territory is disliked; if he takes her out to the abode of Islam, the marriage remains. And the author indicated that it is permissible to have intercourse with a kitabiyyah through right hand possession, and it will come that if a kitabiyyah becomes a Zoroastrian, her marriage to a Muslim is annulled, unlike a Jewess who becomes Christian or vice versa. And al-Usbijabi mentioned that a Muslim can prevent a dhimmi woman if he marries her from going out to churches and monasteries, and he cannot force her to perform ghusl from menstruation or janaba. And in al-Khaniyya from the section on jizya from al-Siyar: A Muslim has a dhimmi wife; he cannot prevent her from drinking wine because wine is halal for her, but he can prevent her from making wine in the house. This is problematic because even though it is halal for her, its smell harms him, so he can prevent her just as a Muslim woman can be prevented from eating garlic and onions. Therefore, al-Kirki in al-Fayd said before the chapter on tayammum: A Muslim can prevent his dhimmi wife from drinking wine just as if a Muslim woman ate garlic and onions and her husband disliked that, he can prevent her. This is the truth as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the permissibility of marrying kitabiyyah (women from the People of the Book, i.e., Jews and Christians). The author begins with the Quranic proof from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:5), which permits marrying chaste women from the People of the Book. He clarifies that 'chaste' is a recommendation, not a condition. He then presents the objection from some (like Ibn Umar) that such women are polytheists because they worship the Messiah and Ezra, and that the verse refers to those who converted to Islam. The majority rebut this by noting that the Quran distinguishes between 'People of the Book' and 'polytheists' in verses such as Surah al-Bayyinah (98:1) and Surah al-Ma'idah (5:82), showing they are separate categories. The author then discusses the definition of 'kitabi': one who believes in a heavenly religion and has a revealed book, including followers of Ibrahim, Seth, and Dawud. This is contrary to al-Shafi'i who restricts it to Jews and Christians. The Hanafi position is that marriage and eating their slaughter are permissible generally. However, there are conditions: some scholars restrict permissibility to those who do not believe in the divinity of the Messiah or Ezra. The preferred view, as in Fath al-Qadir, is that it is absolutely permissible because those who hold such beliefs are extinct groups. The author then discusses the practical rulings: it is better not to marry a kitabiyyah or eat their food except for necessity. Marrying a kitabiyyah from dar al-harb (war territory) is disliked (makruh tanzihi) due to potential negative influence on children. However, if he takes her to dar al-Islam, the marriage continues. The author also addresses the right of a Muslim husband to prevent his dhimmi wife from going to churches, and the issue of preventing her from drinking wine: the correct view is that he can prevent her because its smell harms him, analogous to preventing a Muslim wife from eating garlic. This passage concludes with the statement that this is the truth.

Key Terms
كتابية (kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book, i.e., one who follows a revealed scripture.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following women is NOT considered a kitabiyyah?
A) A Jewish woman
B) A Christian woman
C) A Sabian woman who follows the scriptures of Seth
D) A Zoroastrian woman who does not believe in a prophet

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits marrying all Women of the Book based on Quran 5:5, defining 'kitabi' broadly as anyone with a heavenly book and prophet.

Practical Considerations: Dislike and Conditions in Marrying a Kitabiyyah
Ruling with proofs and intra-Hanafi dispute on conditions and practical recommendations.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the conditions under which marrying a kitabiyyah is disliked and evaluate the intra-Hanafi difference regarding belief in the Trinity.

Core Idea
Though permissible, marrying a kitabiyyah is discouraged due to potential harm, and some Hanafis restrict it if she believes in the divinity of Christ or Ezra.

Beyond the basic permissibility, Hanafi scholars discuss practical concerns: the potential negative influence on children and the prohibition if the woman holds certain polytheistic beliefs. This lesson explores the disliked nature, conditions, and the husband's rights regarding a dhimmi wife.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Karaha (Dislike)
Note that the passage states it is better not to marry a kitabiyyah except for necessity, and this dislike is makruh tanzihi (not haram).
The dislike is based on concern for offspring and faith, not prohibition.
2
Examine the Condition Regarding Belief in Divinity
Some Hanafi scholars (e.g., in al-Mustasfa and al-Mabsoot) restrict permissibility to those who do not believe that the Messiah or Ezra is God. Understand the evidence and the preferred view.
Fath al-Qadir argues that such beliefs are from extinct groups.
3
Distinguish Dar al-Harb vs Dar al-Islam
Marrying a kitabiyyah from dar al-harb is specifically disliked because of the potential for children to adopt the enemy's habits.
If she moves to dar al-Islam, the mariage remains valid.
4
Understand Husband's Rights
A Muslim husband can prevent his dhimmi wife from going to churches and from drinking wine due to harm (smell, etc.).
This is based on qiyas with preventing a Muslim wife from eating garlic.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (وحل تزوج الكتابية لقوله تعالى والمحصنات من الذين أوتوا الكتاب [المائدة: ٥] أي العفائف عن الزنا بياناً للندب لا أن العفة فيهن شرط. وعن ابن عمر أنها لا تحل لأنها مشركة لأنهم يعبدون المسيح وعزيراً، وحمل المحصنات في الآية على من أسلم منهن. وللجمهور أن المشرك ليس من أهل الكتاب للعطف في قوله تعالى لم يكن الذين كفروا من أهل الكتاب والمشركين) [البينة : ١] والعطف يقتضي المغايرة. وفي قوله تعالى لتجدن أشد الناس عداوة للذين آمنوا اليهود والذين أشركوا ﴾ [المائدة: ۸۲] وفي التبيين : ثم كل من يعتقد ديناً سماوياً وله كتاب منزل كصحف إبراهيم وشيث وزبور داود فهو من أهل الكتاب فتجوز مناكحتهم وأكل ذبائحهم خلافاً للشافعي فيما عدا اليهود والنصارى والحجة عليه ما تلونا. وفي فتح القدير: الكتابي من يؤمن بنبي ويقر بكتاب والسامرية من اليهود. أطلق المصنف الكتابية هنا وقيدها في المستصفى بقوله : قالوا هذا يعني الحل إذا لم يعتقد المسيح إلها، أما إذا اعتقده فلا ويوافقه ما في مبسوط شيخ الإسلام ويجب أن لا يأكلوا ذبائح أهل الكتاب إذا اعتقدوا أن المسيح إله وأن عزيراً إله، ولا يتزوجوا نساءهم. قيل : وعليه الفتوى ولكن بالنظر إلى الدلائل ينبغي أنه يجوز الأكل والتزوج ا هـ. وحاصله أن المذهب الإطلاق لما ذكره شمس الأئمة في المبسوط من أن ذبيحة النصراني حلال مطلقاً، سواء قال بثالث ثلاثة أولا لإطلاق الكتاب هنا والدليل. ورجحه في فتح القدير بأن القائل بذلك طائفتان من اليهود والنصارى انقرضوا لا كلهم مع أن مطلق لفظ المشرك إذا ذكر في لسان أهل الشرع لا ينصرف إلى أهل الكتاب وإن صح لغة في طائفة أو طوائف لما عهد من إرادته به من عبد مع الله غيره ممن لا يدعي اتباع نبي وكتاب إلى آخر ما ذكره. وفي معراج الدراية : اختلف العلماء في أن لفظ المشرك يتناول أهل الكتاب والأصح أن اسم المشرك مطلقاً لا يتناوله للعطف في الآية. ثم المشرك ثلاثة : مشرك ظاهراً وباطناً كعبدة الأوثان، ومشرك باطناً لا ظاهراً كالمنافقين ومشرك معنى كأهل الكتاب. ففي قوله سبحانه وتعالى عما يشركون﴾ [يونس : ۱۸] المراد مطلق الشرك، وكذا في قوله تعالى إن الله لا يغفر أن يشرك به ﴾ [النساء : ١١٦] فيتناول جميع الكفار. وفي قوله ولا تنحكوا المشركات) [البقرة : ۲۲۱] المراد به المشرك ظاهراً وباطناً وهو الوثني فلا يتناول أهل الكتاب والمنافقين وأطلقه أيضاً فشمل الكتابية الحرة والأئمة، واتفق الأئمة الأربعة على حل الحرة واختلفوا في حل الأمة كما سيأتي هذا والأولى أن لا يتزوج كتابية ولا يأكل ذبائحهم إلا لضرورة. وفي المحيط : يكره تزوج الكتابية الحربية لأن الإنسان لا يأمن أن يكون بينهما ولد فينشأ على طبائع أهل الحرب ويتخلق بأخلاقهم فلا يستطيع المسلم قلعه عن تلك العادة ا هـ . أنها كراهة تنزية لأن التحريمية لا بد لها من نهي أو ما في معناه لأنها في رتبة الواجب. وفي الخانية : تزوج الحربية مكروه فإن خرج بها إلى دار الإسلام بقي النكاح ا هـ . وأشار المصنف إلى أنه يحل وطء الكتابية بملك اليمين وسيأتي أن الكتابية إذا تمجست فإنه ينفسخ نكاحها من المسلم بخلاف اليهودية إذا تنصرت أو عكسه. وذكر الأسبيجابي أن للمسلم منع الذمية إذا تزوجها من الخروج إلى الكنائس والبيع وليس له إجبارها على الغسل من الحيض والجناية. وفي الخانية من فصل الجزية من السير: مسلم له امرأة ذمية ليس له أن يمنعها من شرب الخمر لأن شرب الخمر حلال عندها وله أن يمنعها عن اتخاذ الخمر في المنزل ا هـ. وهو مشكل لأنه وإن كان حلالاً عندها لكن رائحتها تضره فله منعها كمنع المسلمة من أكل الثوم والبصل ولذا قال الكركي في الفيض قبيل باب التيمم : إن المسلم له أن يمنع زوجته الذمية من شرب الخمر كالمسلمة لو أكلت الثوم والبصل وكان زوجها يكره ذلك له أن يمنعها ا هـ . وهذا هو الحق كما لا يخفى.
His statement: 'And the permissibility of marrying a kitabiyyah (woman of the Book) due to His saying: And the chaste women from those who were given the Book (Quran 5:5) — meaning the chaste ones from fornication, as an indication of recommendation, not that chastity is a condition in them. And from Ibn Umar that she is not permissible because she is a polytheist since they worship the Messiah and Ezra, and he interpreted 'the chaste women' in the verse as those who embraced Islam from them. And for the majority, the polytheist is not from the People of the Book due to the conjunction in His saying: Those who disbelieve from the People of the Book and the polytheists (Quran 98:1) and conjunction requires difference. And in His saying: You will surely find the most hostile of people to the believers are the Jews and those who associate partners (Quran 5:82). And in al-Tabyin: Then everyone who believes in a heavenly religion and has a revealed book like the scriptures of Ibrahim and Seth and the Psalms of Dawud is from the People of the Book, so marrying them is permissible and eating their slaughtered meat is permissible, contrary to al-Shafi'i regarding other than Jews and Christians, and the proof against him is what we have recited. And in Fath al-Qadir: The kitabi is one who believes in a prophet and acknowledges a book, and the Samaritans are from the Jews. The author made the kitabiyyah unrestricted here and restricted it in al-Mustasfa by saying: They said this—meaning the permissibility—if she does not believe that the Messiah is God; if she believes that, then it is not permissible. And this is supported by what is in Mabsoot of Shaykh al-Islam: It is obligatory not to eat the slaughtered meat of the People of the Book if they believe that the Messiah is God and that Ezra is God, and not to marry their women. It is said that the fatwa is upon this, but considering the evidences, it seems that eating and marrying are permissible. The summary is that the madhhab is unrestricted as mentioned by Shams al-A'imma in al-Mabsoot that the slaughtered meat of a Christian is absolutely halal, whether he says Trinity or not, due to the unrestricted nature of the Book and the proof. And he preferred it in Fath al-Qadir because those who say that are two groups from the Jews and Christians who have become extinct, not all of them. Moreover, the unrestricted word 'polytheist' when mentioned in the language of the people of Shari'a does not apply to the People of the Book, even if it is linguistically correct for a group or groups, due to the established usage referring to one who worships other than Allah without claiming to follow a prophet and a book... And in Mi'raj al-Diraya: The scholars differed on whether the word 'polytheist' includes the People of the Book, and the correct view is that the name 'polytheist' absolutely does not include them due to the conjunction in the verse. Then the polytheist is three types: a polytheist outwardly and inwardly like idol worshippers, a polytheist inwardly not outwardly like hypocrites, and a polytheist in meaning like the People of the Book. In His saying: From what they associate (Quran 10:18), the intended meaning is absolute shirk, and similarly in His saying: Indeed, Allah does not forgive that partners be associated with Him (Quran 4:116) includes all disbelievers. And in His saying: And do not marry polytheist women (Quran 2:221), the intended meaning is the polytheist outwardly and inwardly, which is the idol worshipper, so it does not include the People of the Book and the hypocrites. And he also made it unrestricted, so it includes the free kitabiyyah and the slaves. And the four imams agreed on the permissibility of the free one and differed on the permissibility of the slave as will come. And it is better not to marry a kitabiyyah nor to eat their slaughtered meat except for necessity. And in al-Muhit: It is disliked to marry a kitabiyyah from a warring territory because one cannot be sure that a child born between them will grow up with the habits of the people of war and adopt their character, so the Muslim cannot uproot him from that habit. This is a disliked (makruh tanzihi) because the prohibition requires a prohibition or what is in its meaning, as it is in the rank of obligation. And in al-Khaniyya: Marrying a woman from a warring territory is disliked; if he takes her out to the abode of Islam, the marriage remains. And the author indicated that it is permissible to have intercourse with a kitabiyyah through right hand possession, and it will come that if a kitabiyyah becomes a Zoroastrian, her marriage to a Muslim is annulled, unlike a Jewess who becomes Christian or vice versa. And al-Usbijabi mentioned that a Muslim can prevent a dhimmi woman if he marries her from going out to churches and monasteries, and he cannot force her to perform ghusl from menstruation or janaba. And in al-Khaniyya from the section on jizya from al-Siyar: A Muslim has a dhimmi wife; he cannot prevent her from drinking wine because wine is halal for her, but he can prevent her from making wine in the house. This is problematic because even though it is halal for her, its smell harms him, so he can prevent her just as a Muslim woman can be prevented from eating garlic and onions. Therefore, al-Kirki in al-Fayd said before the chapter on tayammum: A Muslim can prevent his dhimmi wife from drinking wine just as if a Muslim woman ate garlic and onions and her husband disliked that, he can prevent her. This is the truth as is not hidden.
Source pages p. 182

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling on the permissibility of marrying kitabiyyah (women from the People of the Book, i.e., Jews and Christians). The author begins with the Quranic proof from Surah al-Ma'idah (5:5), which permits marrying chaste women from the People of the Book. He clarifies that 'chaste' is a recommendation, not a condition. He then presents the objection from some (like Ibn Umar) that such women are polytheists because they worship the Messiah and Ezra, and that the verse refers to those who converted to Islam. The majority rebut this by noting that the Quran distinguishes between 'People of the Book' and 'polytheists' in verses such as Surah al-Bayyinah (98:1) and Surah al-Ma'idah (5:82), showing they are separate categories. The author then discusses the definition of 'kitabi': one who believes in a heavenly religion and has a revealed book, including followers of Ibrahim, Seth, and Dawud. This is contrary to al-Shafi'i who restricts it to Jews and Christians. The Hanafi position is that marriage and eating their slaughter are permissible generally. However, there are conditions: some scholars restrict permissibility to those who do not believe in the divinity of the Messiah or Ezra. The preferred view, as in Fath al-Qadir, is that it is absolutely permissible because those who hold such beliefs are extinct groups. The author then discusses the practical rulings: it is better not to marry a kitabiyyah or eat their food except for necessity. Marrying a kitabiyyah from dar al-harb (war territory) is disliked (makruh tanzihi) due to potential negative influence on children. However, if he takes her to dar al-Islam, the marriage continues. The author also addresses the right of a Muslim husband to prevent his dhimmi wife from going to churches, and the issue of preventing her from drinking wine: the correct view is that he can prevent her because its smell harms him, analogous to preventing a Muslim wife from eating garlic. This passage concludes with the statement that this is the truth.

Key Terms
كتابة (kitabiyyah): A woman from the People of the Book.
كراهة تنزيهية (karaha tanzihiyya): A disliked but not prohibited act; it is better to avoid.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preferred view in the passage, what is the ruling on a Muslim marrying a Christian woman who believes in the Trinity?
A) It is not permissible because she is a polytheist.
B) It is permissible but disliked.
C) It is absolutely permissible without any dislike.
D) It is only permissible if she renounces the Trinity.

Key Takeaway
Marrying a kitabiyyah is permissible but discouraged; the preferred Hanafi view does not condition permissibility on her not believing in the Trinity.
